Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
8 min
The Maxim of Original Innocence (Barā’at al-Dhimmah)
Explains the maxim al-aṣl barā’at al-dhimmah with its furuat and exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim al-aṣl barā’at al-dhimmah to resolve disputes over liability, evidence, and acknowledgments in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
The default is innocence: no claim is proven without solid evidence.

This lesson introduces one of the five major maxims of Hanafi fiqh: al-aṣl barā’at al-dhimmah, meaning the original state is freedom from liability. The maxim governs evidence law, placing the burden of proof on the plaintiff. It is illustrated through a case from Fath al-Qadir about a divorced woman's waiting period, which shows how the original (continuation) is presumed. Then the maxim is stated in Arabic with its key furuat (sub-rulings) and an important exception concerning the minimum number of dirhams in an acknowledgment. Understanding this maxim is essential for issuing correct fatwas in matters of debt, torts, and contracts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the maxim's meaning and scope
The maxim states that a person is presumed free of liability unless proven otherwise. This is a qāʿida kubrā that applies across all fiqh chapters, especially in judiciary and torts.
It derives from the principle of istiṣḥāb (presumption of continuity) and is universally accepted in the school.
2
Identify the furuat from the text
The passage lists four furuat: (1) a single witness is insufficient for liability; (2) the defendant's statement is taken with oath; (3) in disputes over value, the guarantor's statement is accepted; (4) in acknowledgment, the debtor's interpretation of the amount is accepted.
Each furu' directly applies the maxim: the original is non-liability, so any claim must be proven.
3
Analyze the istithnā’ (exception) regarding dirhams
The exception concerns acknowledgment of 'dirhams' absolutely. Although the maxim would suggest interpreting it as the minimum possible (two dirhams based on some linguistic views), the relied-upon Hanafi position is three dirhams, because acknowledgment is built on common usage ('urf), which considers the minimum plural as three.
This shows that the maxim may be overridden by other principles like 'urf and mashhūr.
4
Understand the relationship with other maxims
The maxim is related to 'al-aṣl baqā’ mā kāna ʿalā mā kāna' (original continuity) and 'al-yaqīn lā yazūlu bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt). Together, they provide a consistent framework for handling uncertainty.
In the iddah example, both maxims apply: the original is the continuation of the iddah, and the woman's claim is accepted because it agrees with the original.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Practice: A buyer claims he paid a debt of 100, seller denies receipt. No witnesses. According to barā’at al-dhimmah, the seller is not liable; the buyer must produce evidence. If the buyer acknowledges owing 50 but not 100, the buyer's statement is accepted with oath because the original is freedom from the additional 50.
This illustrates the burden of proof shifting.

قَاعِدَة: الأصْلُ بَرَاءَةُ الذَّمَّةِ وَلِذَا لَمْ يُقْبَلْ فِي شَغْلِهَا شَاهِدٌ وَاحِدٌ وَلِذَا كَانَ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ لِمُوَافَقَتِهِ الأَصْلَ وَ الْبَيِّنَةُ عَلَى الْمُدَّعِي لِدَعْوَاهُ مَا خَالَفَ الأَصْلَ فَإِذَا اخْتَلَفَا فِي قِيْمَةِ الْمُتْلَفِ وَ الْمَغْصُوْبِ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ الْغَارِمِ لأَنَّ الأَصْلَ الْبَرَاءَةُ عَمَّا زَادَ وَ لَوْ أَقَرَّ بِشَيْ أَوْ حَقٌّ قُبِلَ تَفْسِيرُهُ بِمَالَهُ قِيْمَةٌ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْمُقِرٌ مَعَ يَمِيْنِهِ وَلَا يَرِدُ عَلَيْهِ مَا لَوْ أَقَرَّ بِدَرَاهِمَ فَإِنَّهُمْ قَالُوْا تَلْزَمُهُ ثَلَثَةُ دَرَاهِمَ لأَنَّهَا أَقَلُّ الْجَمْعِ مَعَ أَنَّ فِيْهِ اخْتِلَافًا فَقِبْلَ أَقَلُّهُ إثْنَانِ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُحْمَلَ عَلَيْهِ لأَنَّ الأَصْلَ الْبَرَاءَةُ لأَنَّا نَقُوْلُ الْمَشْهُورَ أَنَّهُ ثَلَثَةٌ وَعَلَيْهِ مَبْنَى الإِقْرَارِ.
قَاعِدَةٌ مَنْ شَكَ هَلْ فَعَلَ شَيْئًا أَمْ لَا فَالأَصْلُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَفْعَلْ وَ تَدْخُلُ فِيْهَا قَاعِدَةٌ أُخْرَى مَنْ تَيَقَّنَ الْفِعْلَ وَ شَكٍّ فِي الْقَلِيْلِ وَ الْكَثِيرِ حُمِلَ عَلَى الْقَلِيْلِ لأَنَّهُ الْمُتَيَقَّنُ إِلَّا أَنْ
Translation: If a divorced woman claims that her divorce was prolonged and the waiting period has not ended, she will be believed and she will receive maintenance because the original is the continuation of the waiting period, unless she claims pregnancy, then she is entitled to maintenance for two years. If after two years it becomes known that there is no pregnancy, the husband cannot recover what he paid. This is in Fath al-Qadir.
Explanation: If a divorced woman claims her divorce was prolonged and the waiting period has not ended, she will be believed and get maintenance because the original is continuation. If she claims pregnancy in her womb, she gets maintenance for two years; after two years if it turns out there is no pregnancy, the husband cannot take back what he gave.
Maxim: The original is freedom of the liability. Therefore, a single witness is not accepted to establish a liability. Therefore, the statement of the defendant is accepted because it agrees with the original. The burden of proof is on the plaintiff because his claim contradicts the original. So if they differ over the value of a destroyed or usurped item, the statement of the guarantor (the one liable) is accepted because the original is freedom from an increase. And if one acknowledges something or a right, his interpretation of it as something of value is accepted, so the statement of the acknowledging person with his oath is accepted. This is not contradicted by the case of one who acknowledges dirhams, for they said that three dirhams are incumbent upon him because it is the minimum for a plural, although there is a difference: some said the minimum is two, so it should be interpreted accordingly because the original is freedom. We say: the well-known is that it is three, and acknowledgment is built upon that.
Maxim: Whoever doubts whether he did something or not, the original is that he did not do it. And another maxim enters into it: Whoever is certain of the action and doubts the quantity, small or large, it is taken to be the small amount because it is what is certain, unless...
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of two key Hanafi legal maxims. The author begins with a practical case from Fath al-Qadir: a divorced woman claims her waiting period (iddah) has not ended. The ruling is that she is believed because the original state is the continuation of the iddah. This illustrates the maxim 'al-asl al-baqā' (the original is continuance), which operates in matters of time and status. However, if she claims pregnancy, a different rule applies: she gets maintenance for up to two years, and after that, even if proven false, her husband cannot recover payments—this is due to the operation of istihsan or public interest.

The author then states the central maxim: 'al-asl barā'at al-dhimmah' (the original is freedom from liability). This is one of the five major maxims (al-qawā'id al-kubrā) in Hanafi jurisprudence. Its implications are: (1) a single witness is insufficient to establish liability—two witnesses are required because the default is non-liability; (2) the defendant's statement is accepted with his oath because it agrees with the original, while the plaintiff must bring proof because his claim contradicts the default; (3) in disputes over the value of a damaged or usurped item, the statement of the guarantor (the one who destroyed or usurped) is accepted because the original is freedom from any increase beyond what he admits; (4) if someone acknowledges a debt without specifying, his interpretation (e.g., that it is a small amount) is accepted with his oath, provided his interpretation refers to something of value.

A potential counterexample is raised: if someone acknowledges 'dirhams' absolutely, the Hanafi position is that three dirhams become obligatory because 'dirhams' in common usage implies at least three (the minimum plural). Although some scholars argue the minimum plural is two, the relied-upon position is three because acknowledgment is based on common usage ('urf and mashhūr).

Finally, a related maxim is introduced: 'Whoever doubts whether he did something or not, the original is that he did not do it.' This applies in acts of worship and transactions. And if one is certain of an act but doubts the quantity, the smaller amount is taken because it is certain. This maxim is complementary to barā'at al-dhimmah and governs cases of uncertainty.

Key Terms
براءة الذمة (barā'at al-dhimmah): The legal presumption that a person's liability (dhimmah) is free from any obligation or debt unless proven otherwise.
أصل (aṣl): The default rule or presumption in the absence of evidence to the contrary.
مدعى عليه (mudda'ā ʿalayhi): The defendant, i.e., the person against whom a claim is made.
مدع (mudda'ī): The plaintiff who brings a claim against the defendant.
اقل الجمع (aqall al-jamʿ): The minimum number for a plural, which is three in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The plaintiff's statement
B) The guarantor's (destroyer's) statement
C) The judge's estimate
D) The statement of two witnesses

Key Takeaway
The maxim al-aṣl barā’at al-dhimmah places the burden of proof on the plaintiff and provides default rules for liability disputes, though it may be overridden by established custom in certain cases.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

The Maxim of Doubt in Action and Quantity
Introduces two subsidiary maxims on doubt about action and quantity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxims 'Whoever doubts whether he did something, the original is that he did not do it' and 'Whoever is certain of the action but doubts the quantity, it is taken to be the small amount' to resolve cases of uncertainty in acts of worship and transactions.

Core Idea
Doubt does not override certainty: the original is non-performance and the smaller amount.

This lesson covers two closely related maxims that derive from the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity). The first maxim deals with doubt about whether an action was performed at all: the original is that it was not performed. The second maxim deals with doubt about the quantity after certainty of the action: the smaller certain amount is taken. These maxims are frequently applied in ibadat (e.g., doubt about the number of rak'at in prayer) and muamalat (e.g., doubt about the amount paid). The passage presents them together, noting that the second 'enters into' the first. Understanding these maxims is essential for issuing correct fatwas when evidence is incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two maxims
The first maxim concerns doubt about an action (did I do it or not?). The second concerns certainty about an action but doubt about the quantity (I know I did it, but how many times?). The second is a subset of the first: once you know the action occurred, you doubt the quantity, so you go to the certain minimum.
The passage says the second 'enters into' the first, meaning it is an application of the same principle.
2
Understand the link to istishab
Both maxims rely on istishab: the original state is non-existence (of the action or of the extra quantity). Doubt does not change that original.
This is the same principle behind 'al-yaqīn lā yazūlu bi al-shakk'.
3
Apply to ibadat examples
In prayer: if one doubts whether he prayed four rak'at, the original is that he did not pray the fourth, so he must perform it (unless he is uncertain after completing). In fasting: if one doubts whether he broke his fast before sunset, the original is that he did not, so the fast is valid.
These are standard applications.
4
Apply to muamalat examples
In transactions: if a buyer pays a debt but later doubts whether he paid the full amount, the original is that he did not pay the extra, so he must pay it again unless he is certain he paid. After certainty of payment, if he doubts the quantity (e.g., paid 100 or 200), the smaller amount (100) is taken because it is certain.
The second maxim applies after certainty of the act.
5
Note the exception (incomplete in text)
The passage ends with 'إِلَّا أَنْ' (unless...), indicating there may be exceptions, but the text is cut off. In general, exceptions occur when there is other evidence (e.g., a credible witness) that shifts the presumption.
The mufti should be aware that these maxims can be overridden by stronger evidence.

Source Text

ترجمہ: مطلقہ نے ظہر کے طویل ہونے اور عدت کے پوری نہ ہونے کا دعویٰ کیا تو اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی اور اس کے لئے نفقہ ہو گا اس لئے اصل اس (عدت ) کا باقی رہنا ہے الا یہ کہ وہ عمل کا دھوٹی کرے تو وہ دو سال تک نفقہ کی مستحق ہے اور اگر دو سال گذرنے پر پتہ چلا کہ مل ہی نہیں ہے تو اس پر رجوع نہیں کیا جائے گا فتح القدیر میں ایسا ہی ہے ۔
تشریح مطلقہ عورت نے دعوی کیا کہ میر اطہر لمبا ہو گیا اور ابھی عدت نہیں گذری ہے تو اس کی بات مانی جائے گی اور اس کو نفقہ بھی ملے گا اس لئے کہ اصل چیز بقاء ہے۔ إلا إذا إدعت الحيل : مطلقہ اپنے پیٹ میں اپنے شوہر کے حمل کا دعویٰ کرے تو اس کو دو سال تک نفقہ ملے گا اگر دو سال گذر گئے پھر معلوم ہوا کہ حمل نہیں ہے تو ایسی صورت میں شو ہر اپنا دیا ہوا واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔
قَاعِدَة: الأصْلُ بَرَاءَةُ الذَّمَّةِ وَلِذَا لَمْ يُقْبَلْ فِي شَغْلِهَا شَاهِدٌ وَاحِدٌ وَلِذَا كَانَ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ لِمُوَافَقَتِهِ الأَصْلَ وَ الْبَيِّنَةُ عَلَى الْمُدَّعِي لِدَعْوَاهُ مَا خَالَفَ الأَصْلَ فَإِذَا اخْتَلَفَا فِي قِيْمَةِ الْمُتْلَفِ وَ الْمَغْصُوْبِ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ الْغَارِمِ لأَنَّ الأَصْلَ الْبَرَاءَةُ عَمَّا زَادَ وَ لَوْ أَقَرَّ بِشَيْ أَوْ حَقٌّ قُبِلَ تَفْسِيرُهُ بِمَالَهُ قِيْمَةٌ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْمُقِرٌ مَعَ يَمِيْنِهِ وَلَا يَرِدُ عَلَيْهِ مَا لَوْ أَقَرَّ بِدَرَاهِمَ فَإِنَّهُمْ قَالُوْا تَلْزَمُهُ ثَلَثَةُ دَرَاهِمَ لأَنَّهَا أَقَلُّ الْجَمْعِ مَعَ أَنَّ فِيْهِ اخْتِلَافًا فَقِبْلَ أَقَلُّهُ إثْنَانِ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُحْمَلَ عَلَيْهِ لأَنَّ الأَصْلَ الْبَرَاءَةُ لأَنَّا نَقُوْلُ الْمَشْهُورَ أَنَّهُ ثَلَثَةٌ وَعَلَيْهِ مَبْنَى الإِقْرَارِ.
قَاعِدَةٌ مَنْ شَكَ هَلْ فَعَلَ شَيْئًا أَمْ لَا فَالأَصْلُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَفْعَلْ وَ تَدْخُلُ فِيْهَا قَاعِدَةٌ أُخْرَى مَنْ تَيَقَّنَ الْفِعْلَ وَ شَكٍّ فِي الْقَلِيْلِ وَ الْكَثِيرِ حُمِلَ عَلَى الْقَلِيْلِ لأَنَّهُ الْمُتَيَقَّنُ إِلَّا أَنْ
Translation: If a divorced woman claims that her divorce was prolonged and the waiting period has not ended, she will be believed and she will receive maintenance because the original is the continuation of the waiting period, unless she claims pregnancy, then she is entitled to maintenance for two years. If after two years it becomes known that there is no pregnancy, the husband cannot recover what he paid. This is in Fath al-Qadir.
Explanation: If a divorced woman claims her divorce was prolonged and the waiting period has not ended, she will be believed and get maintenance because the original is continuation. If she claims pregnancy in her womb, she gets maintenance for two years; after two years if it turns out there is no pregnancy, the husband cannot take back what he gave.
Maxim: The original is freedom of the liability. Therefore, a single witness is not accepted to establish a liability. Therefore, the statement of the defendant is accepted because it agrees with the original. The burden of proof is on the plaintiff because his claim contradicts the original. So if they differ over the value of a destroyed or usurped item, the statement of the guarantor (the one liable) is accepted because the original is freedom from an increase. And if one acknowledges something or a right, his interpretation of it as something of value is accepted, so the statement of the acknowledging person with his oath is accepted. This is not contradicted by the case of one who acknowledges dirhams, for they said that three dirhams are incumbent upon him because it is the minimum for a plural, although there is a difference: some said the minimum is two, so it should be interpreted accordingly because the original is freedom. We say: the well-known is that it is three, and acknowledgment is built upon that.
Maxim: Whoever doubts whether he did something or not, the original is that he did not do it. And another maxim enters into it: Whoever is certain of the action and doubts the quantity, small or large, it is taken to be the small amount because it is what is certain, unless...
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of two key Hanafi legal maxims. The author begins with a practical case from Fath al-Qadir: a divorced woman claims her waiting period (iddah) has not ended. The ruling is that she is believed because the original state is the continuation of the iddah. This illustrates the maxim 'al-asl al-baqā' (the original is continuance), which operates in matters of time and status. However, if she claims pregnancy, a different rule applies: she gets maintenance for up to two years, and after that, even if proven false, her husband cannot recover payments—this is due to the operation of istihsan or public interest.

The author then states the central maxim: 'al-asl barā'at al-dhimmah' (the original is freedom from liability). This is one of the five major maxims (al-qawā'id al-kubrā) in Hanafi jurisprudence. Its implications are: (1) a single witness is insufficient to establish liability—two witnesses are required because the default is non-liability; (2) the defendant's statement is accepted with his oath because it agrees with the original, while the plaintiff must bring proof because his claim contradicts the default; (3) in disputes over the value of a damaged or usurped item, the statement of the guarantor (the one who destroyed or usurped) is accepted because the original is freedom from any increase beyond what he admits; (4) if someone acknowledges a debt without specifying, his interpretation (e.g., that it is a small amount) is accepted with his oath, provided his interpretation refers to something of value.

A potential counterexample is raised: if someone acknowledges 'dirhams' absolutely, the Hanafi position is that three dirhams become obligatory because 'dirhams' in common usage implies at least three (the minimum plural). Although some scholars argue the minimum plural is two, the relied-upon position is three because acknowledgment is based on common usage ('urf and mashhūr).

Finally, a related maxim is introduced: 'Whoever doubts whether he did something or not, the original is that he did not do it.' This applies in acts of worship and transactions. And if one is certain of an act but doubts the quantity, the smaller amount is taken because it is certain. This maxim is complementary to barā'at al-dhimmah and governs cases of uncertainty.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Doubt or uncertainty about a matter of fact.
تيقن (tayaqqun): Certainty established by evidence or clear knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim from this lesson, what is the ruling if a person doubts whether he performed a given action?
A) He must assume he performed it because the original is existence.
B) He must assume he did not perform it because the original is non-existence.
C) He must repeat the action to be safe.
D) He must seek a witness to confirm.

Key Takeaway
When in doubt about an action, assume it did not happen; when certain of the action but unsure of the quantity, take the smallest certain amount.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate

Maxim of Doubt: Original Presumption of Non-Performance
Explaining the maxim about doubt in action and its sub-maxims with a Hanafi fiqh example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'man shakka hal fa'ala shay'an am la' to determine rulings in cases of doubt, identify the embedded sub-maxim about quantity, and recognize the exception when liability is occupied by an established obligation.

Core Idea
When in doubt about an act, presume it was not done; but a certain obligation is removed only by certainty.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi legal maxim from Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair governing doubt in actions. The maxim establishes a default presumption of non-performance, but it is qualified by sub-maxims: one about quantity (the minimum is certain) and an exception when liability is already established. We will explore these through fiqh examples and the practical fatwa from Al-Multaqat.

Guided Path
1
State the Main Maxim
Read the Arabic: 'من شك هل فعل شيئا أم لا فالأصل أنه لم يفعل'. Understand that when a person is uncertain whether they performed an act, the original legal presumption is that they did not do it.
This applies to both acts of worship and transactions.
2
Identify the Sub-Maxim on Quantity
The passage states: if one is certain of performing the act but doubts the amount (little or much), adopt the minimum because it is certain. This is an application of the same principle: the certain minimum prevails over doubt about excess.
E.g., praying three or four rak'ahs: build on three.
3
Recognize the Exception: Liability Occupied
The exception: if the person's liability is already occupied by an established obligation (e.g., a definite debt or missed prayer), doubt does not remove it. The principle 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يرفع إلا بيقين' applies: certainty is needed to discharge.
The exception overrides the default presumption.
4
Apply to the Al-Multaqat Example
The text cites: if a person has no definite missed prayer but doubts past validity, making up prayers is not recommended unless there is predominant conjecture (غالب الظن) of defect. Only those prayers likely invalid should be qada'.
Predominant conjecture here has force of certainty.
5
Note the Epistemological Nuance
In the Hanafi qawida, 'doubt' includes both equal hesitation and predominant conjecture, though usuliyun differentiate. The exception requires 'certainty', which in practice means predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann).
This aligns with the Hanafi principle of taking predominant conjecture as certain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَاعِدَةٌ مَنْ شَكَ هَلْ فَعَلَ شَيْئًا أَمْ لَا فَالأَصْلُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَفْعَلْ وَ تَدْخُلُ فِيْهَا قَاعِدَةٌ أُخْرَى مَنْ تَيَقَّنَ الْفِعْلَ وَ شَكٍّ فِي الْقَلِيْلِ وَ الْكَثِيرِ حُمِلَ عَلَى الْقَلِيْلِ لأَنَّهُ الْمُتَيَقَّنُ إِلَّا أَنْ تَشْتَهِلَ الذِمَةُ بالْأَصْل فَلَا يَبْرَأ إلَّا باليَقِينِ وَهَذَا الاسْتِكْنَاءُ رَاجِعٌ إِلَى قَاعِدَة ثانية هي ما تَبَتْ بِيَقِينٍ لَا يَرْتَفِعُ إِلَّا بِيَقِينٍ والمراد به غَالِبُ الظَّن.
ترجمہ : قاعدہ جس شخص کو یہ یہ ہوا کس نے کوئی کام کیا ہے یانہیں؟ تواصل یہ ہے کہ اس نے کہانی کی اور اس میں ایک دوسرا قاعدہ داخل ہے جس کو کام کرنے کا یقین ہے اور تیل و کثیر میں شک ہے تو صیل پر میاں کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ متقین ہے مگر اصل فعل کے ساتھ ذمہ مشغول ہے تو اس سے یقین ہی کے ذریعہ بری ہوگا وہ ہیں استثناء ایک تیسرے قاعدہ کی طرف راجح ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ جو امر یقین سے ثابت ہو وہ یقین سے ہی مرتفع ہوگا اور اس سے مراد غالب ظن ہے۔
تشریح: ایک شخص کو شک ہے کہ اس نے فلاں کام کیا ہے یا نہیں تو ایسی صورت میں اصل چیز یہ ہے کہ ان نے یہ کام نہیں کیا ہے اور فقہاء کے نزدیک شک اس بات کا نام ہے کہ کسی کو کسی چیز کے وجود اور عدم وجود میں زوردی خواہ دونوں طرف تردد میں برابر ہو یا ایک راجح ہو لیکن اصولین کے نزدیک استقواء الطرفین کا نام ہے اگر ایک جانب راج اور دوسری مرجوح ہو تو راج کو ظن اور مرجوح کو وہم کہتے ہیں۔ وتدخل فيها قاعدة اخرى: کسی شخص کو فعل کے کرنے کا تو یقین ہے لیکن قلیل و کثیر میں شک ہے ان کی صورت میں چونکہ قلیل کا کرنا متیقن ہی ہے لہذا اقلیل پر محمول کیا جائے گا ہاں اگر ذمہ اصل فعل کے کرنے نہ کرنے کے ساتھ مشغول ہو جائے تو ایسی صورت میں بغیر یقین کے وہ شخص بری الذمہ ہوگا۔ ما ثبت بيقين لا يرفع الا بیقین: ایک شخص کو کسی چیز کے وجود میں یقین ہو تو ایسی صورت میں اس کا بنیں اس وقت تک زائل نہیں ہو سکتا جب تک اس چیز کے عدم کا یقین ہو جائے ۔ والمراد به غالب الظن : یقین سے مراد یہاں غالب گمان ہے یعنی خواہ اس کے خلاف کا وہم ہو پھر بھی ان گمان کو یقین کے درجہ میں رکھا جائے گا۔ وَلِذَا قَالَ فِي الْمُلْتَقَطِ وَلَوْ لَمْ يَفْتْهُ مِنَ الصَّلواةِ شَيٍّ وَ أَحَبَّ أَنْ يَقْضِيَ صَلوةَ عُمْرِهِ مُنْذُ ادْرَكَ لَا يَسْتَحِبُّ ذَلِكَ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ اكْبَرَ ظَنِّهِ فَسَادَهَا بِسَلْبِ الطَّهَارَةِ أَو تَرْكِ شَرْطٍ فَحِيْنَئِذٍ يَقْضِيْ مَا غَلَبْ عَلَى ظَنّهِ وَ مَا زَادَ عَلَيْهِ يَكْرَهُ لِوُرُوْدِ النَّهْي عَنْهُ إِنْتَهى
Rule: Whoever doubts whether he did something or not, the original state is that he did not do it. And another rule enters into it: whoever is certain of the act but doubts about the little or the many, it is taken to the little because it is the certain one, unless the liability is occupied by the original (obligation), in which case he is not released except by certainty. This exception goes back to a third rule: what is established by certainty is not removed except by certainty. And what is meant by it is predominant conjecture. Commentary: A person doubts whether he performed a certain action or not; in such a case the original thing is that he did not do it. According to jurists, doubt is when a person is hesitant between existence and non-existence, whether both sides are equal or one is preponderant. But according to usuliyyun, doubt is equal hesitation; if one side is preponderant, it is called zann (conjecture) and the other wahm (whim). And another rule enters into it: a person is certain of performing the act but doubts whether it was little or much; in such a case, since the minimum is certain, it is interpreted as the minimum. Yes, if the liability is occupied by the original act (i.e., the act itself creates an obligation), then he is not released except by certainty. 'What is established by certainty is not removed except by certainty': a person is certain of the existence of something; then that certainty cannot be removed until certainty of non-existence occurs. And what is meant by it is predominant conjecture: i.e., even if there is a possibility of the opposite, that predominant conjecture is considered as certainty. Therefore it is said in Al-Multaqat: If no prayer has been missed from him, and he wishes to make qada' of the prayers of his entire life since puberty, that is not recommended unless his predominant conjecture is that they were corrupt due to lack of purity or leaving a condition. In that case, he makes qada' according to his predominant conjecture, and what is beyond that is disliked because prohibition has come against it. End.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage presents a major qawida (maxim) of Hanafi jurisprudence: 'Whoever doubts whether he did something or not, the original state is that he did not do it.' This maxim governs issues of doubt in acts of worship and transactions. Two sub-maxims are embedded: (1) If one is certain of performing an act but doubts the quantity, the minimum is adopted because it is certain. (2) Exception: if the act-based obligation (e.g., a debt or missed prayer) has been established by certainty, then it is not removed except by certainty (المتيقن لا يزول بالشك). In this context, 'certainty' means predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann), not absolute certainty. The commentary distinguishes between doubt proper (equal hesitation) and predominant conjecture (zann) according to the usuliyun, but in the Hanafi qawida, 'doubt' includes both. The example from Al-Multaqat illustrates: if one has no missed prayer but doubts the validity of past prayers due to possible defects (missing purity or conditions), then making up those prayers is not recommended unless there is predominant conjecture of invalidity. Only those prayers that are predominantly conjectured to be invalid should be made up; doing more is makruh because of the prohibition of unnecessary qada'.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Hesitation between existence and non-existence of a matter; in this context it includes both equal doubt and preponderant conjecture, though usuliyun differentiate.
ظن غالب (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant conjecture that has the legal force of certainty in removing doubt or establishing obligation.
متیقن (mutayaqqan): What is certain; in the context of doubt about quantity, it refers to the minimum that is definitely established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is certain he missed his Fajr prayer but doubts whether he missed one or two rak'ahs. According to the Hanafi maxim, what should he do?
A) Pray two rak'ahs because that is the original obligation
B) Pray one rak'ah because that is the minimum certain
C) He does not need to pray because doubt excuses
D) Pray two rak'ahs plus the sunnah

Key Takeaway
When in doubt about an act, presume it was not done; but a certain obligation is removed only by certainty (predominant conjecture).

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

The Maxim: Certainty is Not Removed by Doubt
Definition and expansion of the maxim with legal clarification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يرفع إلا بيقين' to identify when overwhelming presumption (ghālib al-ẓann) suffices to establish a ruling, and evaluate its application in the case of qada' umri.

Core Idea
Certainty in Hanafi law includes overwhelming presumption — a strong doubt cannot undo a certain ruling.

This lesson unpacks one of the five major legal maxims (al-qawāʿid al-kulliyya al-kubrā) in the Hanafi school: 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يرفع إلا بيقين' — what is established by certainty is not removed except by certainty. The author explains that 'certainty' here does not refer to absolute certainty (which is rare in legal reasoning), but to overwhelming presumption (ghālib al-ẓann). This maxim governs a vast range of fiqh rulings, from purity to contracts. We will explore its definition, its relation to other maxims, and its concrete application in the issue of making up missed prayers (qada' umri).

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its core meaning
Read the opening Arabic: 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يرفع إلا بيقين'. Note the key terms: 'thabata' (established), 'yaqīn' (certainty), 'yarfaʿ' (removed). Understand that the maxim says a legal state proven with certainty cannot be overturned by mere doubt.
The author immediately adds that 'certainty' here means ghālib al-ẓann (overwhelming presumption), not absolute certainty.
2
Distinguish the three maxims in the passage
The passage weaves three maxims: (1) الأصل بقاء ما كان على ما كان (things persist as they were) – the ruling on liability, (2) If certain of an act but doubtful of its quantity, presume the lesser, (3) The main maxim: certainty is only removed by certainty. Trace how each appears in the text.
The second maxim is not named but implied: 'if one is certain of performing an act but doubts its quantity, the lesser is presumed'.
3
Analyze the legal definition of yaqīn in this context
The author redefines yaqīn as ghālib al-ẓann. Use the legal definition dissector: term=اليقين, locus=any ruling established by certainty, cause=evidence or overwhelming presumption, condition=not contradicted by equal certainty, effect=ruling remains until removed by equal or stronger certainty.
This is a key Hanafi departure from other schools that require absolute yaqīn.
4
Apply the maxim to the furuʿ case of qada' umri
The example from al-Multaqat: a person who never missed a prayer but wants to make up all prayers from puberty. The ruling: not recommended unless overwhelming presumption that prayers were invalid due to missing purity or conditions. Then only make up those for which ghālib al-ẓann exists; extra is disliked.
The maxim operates here: the original certainty (prayers are valid) is not removed by mere doubt; only overwhelming presumption of invalidity can overturn.
5
Evaluate the istithnā' (exception) when liability is occupied
The author notes an exception: if liability is already established (e.g., debt confirmed), it is not absolved except by certainty. This invokes the maxim 'الأصل شغل الذمة' (the original state is liability). The exception confirms the rule: certainty is needed to clear a certain liability.
The exception is not a contradiction but a parallel application of the same principle.

Source Text

قبت بيقين لا يَرْتَفِعُ إلَّا بيقين و المراد به غَالِبُ الظَّن. تَشْتَهِل الذمة بالأصل فلا يبرأ إلا باليقين وهذا الاسْتِكْنَاءُ رَاجِعُ إِلَى قَاعِدَة ثانية هي ما ترجمہ : قاعدہ جس شخص کو یہ یہ ہوا کس نے کوئی کام کیا ہے یانہیں؟ تواصل یہ ہے کہ اس نے کہانی کی اور اس میں ایک دوسرا قاعدہ داخل ہے جس کو کام کرنے کا یقین ہے اور تیل و کثیر میں شک ہے تو صیل پر میاں کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ متقین ہے مگر اصل فعل کے ساتھ ذمہ مشغول ہے تو اس سے یقین ہی کے ذریعہ بری ہوگا وہ ہیں استثناء ایک تیسرے قاعدہ کی طرف راجح ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ جو امر یقین سے ثابت ہو وہ یقین سے ہی مرتفع ہوگا اور اس سے مراد غالب ظن ہے۔ تشریح: ایک شخص کو شک ہے کہ اس نے فلاں کام کیا ہے یا نہیں تو ایسی صورت میں اصل چیز یہ ہے کہ ان نے یہ کام نہیں کیا ہے اور فقہاء کے نزدیک شک اس بات کا نام ہے کہ کسی کو کسی چیز کے وجود اور عدم وجود میں زوردی خواہ دونوں طرف تردد میں برابر ہو یا ایک راجح ہو لیکن اصولین کے نزدیک استقواء الطرفین کا نام ہے اگر ایک جانب راج اور دوسری مرجوح ہو تو راج کو ظن اور مرجوح کو وہم کہتے ہیں۔ وتدخل فيها قاعدة اخرى: کسی شخص کو فعل کے کرنے کا تو یقین ہے لیکن قلیل و کثیر میں شک ہے ان کی صورت میں چونکہ قلیل کا کرنا متیقن ہی ہے لہذا اقلیل پر محمول کیا جائے گا ہاں اگر ذمہ اصل فعل کے کرنے نہ کرنے کے ساتھ مشغول ہو جائے تو ایسی صورت میں بغیر یقین کے وہ شخص بری الذمہ ہوگا۔ ما ثبت بيقين لا يرفع الا بیقین: ایک شخص کو کسی چیز کے وجود میں یقین ہو تو ایسی صورت میں اس کا بنیں اس وقت تک زائل نہیں ہو سکتا جب تک اس چیز کے عدم کا یقین ہو جائے ۔ والمراد به غالب الظن : یقین سے مراد یہاں غالب گمان ہے یعنی خواہ اس کے خلاف کا وہم ہو پھر بھی ان گمان کو یقین کے درجہ میں رکھا جائے گا۔ وَلِذَا قَالَ فِي الْمُلْتَقَطِ وَلَوْ لَمْ يَفْتْهُ مِنَ الصَّلواةِ شَيٍّ وَ أَحَبَّ أَنْ يَقْضِيَ صَلوةَ عُمْرِهِ مُنْذُ ادْرَكَ لَا يَسْتَحِبُّ ذَلِكَ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ اكْبَرَ ظَنَّهُ فَسَادَهَا بِسَلْبِ الطَّهَارَةِ أَو تَرْكِ شَرْطٍ فَحِيْنَئِذٍ يَقْضِيْ مَا غَلَبْ عَلَى ظَنّهِ وَ مَا زَادَ عَلَيْهِ يَكْرَهُ لِوُرُوْدِ النَّهْي عَنْهُ إِنْتَهى ترجمه اور اسی وجہ سے ملتقط میں ہے اور اگر اس کی کوئی نماز نہیں چھوٹی اور وہ بالغ ہونے کے وقت سے اپنی پوری عمر کی نماز میں قضا کرنی چاہے تو یہ اس کے لئے پسندیدہ نہیں ہے الا یہ کہ طہارت نہ ہونے یا کسی شرط کے چھوٹ جانے کی وجہ سے ان کے فاسد ہونے کا اسے غالب گمان ہو تو ایسی صورت میں اپنے غالب گمان کے مطابق قضا کرے اور جواس ( گمان غالب) سے زائد ہوں (ان کی قضا ) مکروہ ہے اس پر نبی وارد ہونے کی وجہ سے ملت کا کام پر ہو یکر اب تک کوئی نماز فوت نہیں ہوئی ہے اور وہ شخص قضاء عمری ادا کرنا چاہے تو اس کے لئے قضاء عمری مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح: چونکہ یقین شک سے ختم نہیں ہوتا اور یقین سے مرادخل بہ بیکن ہے لہذا ایک شخص کی بالغ ہونے سے إلا إذا كان اكبر طنه: جس شخص کو غالب گمان ہے کہ اس کی بعض نماز میں طہارت کے مفقود ہونے کی وجہ سے یا شرط کے ترک کی وجہ سے فاسد ہو گئی تھیں تو ایسی صورت میں جن نمازوں کے بارے میں غالب گمان ہوا ان کی تقاء کرے لیکن اگر غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ اس کی نمازیں قضاء نہیں میں پھر بھی وہ قضاء کرے تو اسکی صورت میں قضاء عربی مگر وہ ہے کیونکہ اس سے حدیث میں منع کیا گیا ہے۔
What is established by certainty is not removed except by certainty, and what is meant by it is overwhelming presumption. The liability is occupied by the original [state], so it is not absolved except by certainty, and this exception refers to a second rule... [Urdu translation and commentary]
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the maxim 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يرفع إلا بيقين' (What is established by certainty is not removed except by certainty). The author explains that 'certainty' here means overwhelming presumption (ghālib al-ẓann). He then discusses two related maxims: (1) The original ruling is that a person is not held liable for an act unless proven; (2) If one is certain of performing an act but doubts its quantity, the lesser amount is presumed. The third maxim (the main one) states that a certainty is only removed by certainty. The author illustrates this with the example from al-Multaqat: a person who has never missed a prayer is not encouraged to perform qada' umri (making up all prayers from puberty) unless he has an overwhelming presumption that his prayers were invalid due to lack of purity or missing a condition. In that case, he only makes up those prayers for which he has such presumption; doing more is disliked due to prophetic prohibition. This shows that overwhelming presumption is treated as certainty in legal rulings.

Key Terms
يَقِين (yaqīn): Certainty; in this text, it includes overwhelming presumption (ghālib al-ẓann) for legal purposes.
غَالِب الظَّن (ghālib al-ẓann): Overwhelming presumption; a strong belief that outweighs doubt.
قَاعِدَة (qā‘idah): A legal maxim that governs many particular cases.
شَكّ (shakk): Doubt; in this passage, jurists include both equal doubt and preponderance, while usul scholars restrict it to equal probability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what meaning of 'certainty' (yaqīn) is intended in the maxim 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يرفع إلا بيقين'?
A) Absolute certainty with no doubt whatsoever
B) Overwhelming presumption (ghālib al-ẓann)
C) The testimony of two male witnesses
D) The majority opinion of scholars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'ما ثبت بيقين لا يرفع إلا بيقين' governs that a ruling established by certainty (including gi'lib al-ẓann) remains in effect until overturned by equal or stronger certainty.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
10 min
Certainty is not removed by doubt: Application to Prayer Doubts
Applying 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to specific prayer doubts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (اليقين لا يزول بالشك) to various scenarios of doubt in prayer and state the correct ruling for each case.

Core Idea
Certainty is the default; doubt only triggers action during the act, not after.

One of the five great maxims of Islamic jurisprudence is 'Certainty is not removed by doubt.' This principle serves as the foundation for many rulings in Salah, especially when a worshipper experiences uncertainty about actions or rak'at. In this lesson, we will explore how classical Hanafi jurists applied this maxim to specific prayer doubts, distinguishing between doubts that occur during prayer, after prayer, and for frequent doubters. By mastering these applications, you will be able to resolve common fiqhi questions with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing maxim
Recognise that all the rulings in this passage derive from the qawida 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk'. Understand that yaqin (certainty) is the default state, and shakk (doubt) does not overturn it.
The maxim is stated in the source's opening discussion on qada' umri.
2
Categorise the timing of the doubt
For each ruling, note whether the doubt occurs during the prayer (fi al-salah) or after completion (ba'd al-faragh). The ruling differs: during the prayer, one must act; after, doubt is generally ignored.
The source specifies: 'إذا شك فيها قبل الفراغ' vs 'إذا كان بعد الفراغ'.
3
Apply the specific rule for each scenario
Work through each furu' (branch) mentioned: doubt about performing the prayer, doubt about a specific action, doubt about rak'at, and so on. For each, state the ruling and explain how the maxim leads to it.
Pay attention to the exception for frequent doubters (kathir al-shakk) who use taharri.
4
Determine the mufta bihi for a given case
After understanding the rulings, practice constructing a fatwa based on the maxim. For a new scenario, identify whether the doubt is before or after completion, whether the person is a frequent doubter, and apply the appropriate rule.
The source includes cases like informant after salam and imam-congregation disagreement.

یکر اب تک کوئی نماز فوت نہیں ہوئی ہے اور وہ شخص قضاء عمری ادا کرنا چاہے تو اس کے لئے قضاء عمری مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح: چونکہ یقین شک سے ختم نہیں ہوتا اور یقین سے مرادخل بہ بیکن ہے لہذا ایک شخص کی بالغ ہونے سے إلا إذا كان اكبر طنه: جس شخص کو غالب گمان ہے کہ اس کی بعض نماز میں طہارت کے مفقود ہونے کی وجہ سے یا شرط کے ترک کی وجہ سے فاسد ہو گئی تھیں تو ایسی صورت میں جن نمازوں کے بارے میں غالب گمان ہوا ان کی تقاء کرے لیکن اگر غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ اس کی نمازیں قضاء نہیں میں پھر بھی وہ قضاء کرے تو اسکی صورت میں قضاء عربی مگر وہ ہے کیونکہ اس سے حدیث میں منع کیا گیا ہے۔
تَكَّ فِي صَلَوَةٍ هَلْ صَلَّاهَا أَمْ لَا أَعَادَ فِي الْوَقْتِ. شَكٍّ فِي رُكُوْعٍ أَوْسُجُوْدٍ وَهُوَ فِيْهَا الْعَادَ وَإِنْ كَانَ يَعْدَهَا فَلَا وَ إِنْ شَكَ أَنَّهُ كَمْ صَلَى فَإِنْ كَانَ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ إِسْتَأْنَفَ وَ إِنْ كَثُرَ تَحْوَى وَ إِلَّا أَخَذَ بِالأَقَلِّ وَهَذَا إِذَا شَكٍّ فِيْهَا قَبْلَ الْفَرَاغِ وَ إِنْ كَانَ بَعْدَهُ فَلَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا إِذَا تَذَكَّرَ بَعْدَ الْفَرَاغِ أَنَّهُ تَرَكَ فَرْضًا وَ شَكٍّ فِي تَعْيِنِهِ قَالُوْا يَسْجُدُ سَجْدَةً وَاحِدَةً ثُمَّ يَقْعُدُ ثُمَّ يَقُوْمُ فَيُصَلِّى رَكْعَةً بِسَجْدَتَيْنِ ثُمَّ يَقْعُدُ ثُمَّ يَسْجُدُ لِلسَّهْوِ كَذَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيْرِ. ترجمه کسی نماز کے بارے میں شک ہوا کہ وہ نماز پڑھ لی ہے یا نہیں تو اس کے وقت میں اس کو لوٹالے کسی رکوع یا سجد ہ میں شک ہوا حالانکہ وہ اس (نماز) ہی میں ہے تو اس کو لوٹالے اور اگر (شک )اس ( نماز ۹ کے بعد ہو نہ لوٹائے اور اگر شک ہوا کہ اس نے کتنی رکعت پڑھی ہیں تو اگر یہ پہلی مرتبہ ہوا تو از سر نو پڑھ لے اور اگر اکثر ایسا بھی ہو تو تری کرے رونہ پھر کم کو اختیار کرے اور یہ اس صورت میں ہے جب شک نماز پوری کرنے سے پہلے ہو اور مانیا (نماز) کے بعد ہو تو اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں الا یہ کہ فارغ ہو جانے کے بعد یاد آجائے کہ کوئی فرض چھوڑا ہے اور اس کی تعین میں شک ہو تو فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک سجدہ کرے پھر بیٹھ جائے پھر کھڑا ہو پھر دوسجدوں کے ساتھ ایک بہت پڑھے پھر بیٹھ جائے پھر سجدہ سہو کرے کذافی فتح القدیر تشریح: ایک شخص کو نماز کے ادا کرنے میں شک ہو گیا کہ ادا کر لی ہے یا نہیں ؟ تو اگر وقت باقی ہے اس نماز کا اعادہ کرے۔
شک فی رکوع أو سجود : ایک شخص کو دورانِ نماز رکوع کے یا سجدہ کے بارے میں شک ہو گیا کہ کیا ہے نہیں تو ایسی صورت میں نماز کے اندر اعادہ کر لے اگر نماز پڑھ چکا ہے تو اعادہ کی ضرورت نہیں۔ فإن شک انه کم صلی : ایک شخص کو شک ہو گیا کہ اس نے کتنی رکعتیں پڑھی ہیں تو ایسی صورت میں اگر پہلی منہاس کو یہ بات پیش آئی ہے تو دوبارہ نماز پڑھ لے اگر بار بار ایسا ہوتا ہے تو پھر تحری کر کے غالب گمان پر عمل کرے عید کر کسی ایک جانب گمان غالب نہ ہوتا ہو تو اقل کو اختیار کرے اور بقیہ کو پورا کرے یہ اس صورت میں ہے کہ جبکہ نماز سے فارغ ہونے سے پہلے شک ہوا ہو اور اگر وہ نماز پڑھ چکا ہے تو اس کے ذمہ کچھ بھی واجب نہیں ہے۔ ـد الفراغ : ایک شخص کو نماز پڑھ لینے کے بعد یاد آیا کہ اس نے نماز کا کوئی فرض مشتار کو ٹ یا سجدہ چھوڑ دیا ہے لیکن یہ معلوم نہیں کہ کونسا چھوڑا ہے تو ایسی صورت میں یہ شخص ایک سجدہ کرے پھر قعدہ کرے پھر کھڑا ہو کر ایک پوری رکعت ادا کرے اور آخر میں سجدہ سہو بھی کرے۔
وَلَوْ أَخْبَرَهُ عَدْلٌ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ أَنَّكَ صَلَّيْتَ الظُّهْرَ أَرْبَعاً وَ شَكٍّ فِي صِدْقِهِ وَ كِذْبِهِ فَإِنَّهَ يُعِيدُ إختِيَاطًا لأَنَّ الشَّكَ فِي صِدْقِهِ شَكٍّ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَلَوْ وَقَعَ الإِخْتِلَافُ بَيْنَ الْإِمَامِ وَ الْقَوْمِ فَإِنْ كَانَ الإِمَامُ عَلَى يَقِيْنِ لَا يُعِيدُ وَ إِنْ لَّا أَعَادَ بِقَوْلِهِمْ كَذَا فِي الْخُلَاصَةِ وَلَوْ صَلَى رَكْعَةً بِييَّةِ الظُّهْرِ ثُمَّ شَكٍّ فِي الثَّانِيَةِ أَنَّهُ فِي الْعَصْرِ ثُمَّ شَكٍّ فِي الثَّالِثَةِ أَنَّهُ فِي التَّطَوُّع ثُمَّ شَكٍّ فِي الرَّابِعَةِ أَنَّهُ فِي الظُّهْرِ قَالُوْا يَكُوْنُ فِي الظُّهْرِ وَالشَّكُ لَيْسَ بِشَيْ. ترجمه: سلام پھیرنے کے بعد کسی عادل آدمی نے اسے خبر دی کہ آپ نے ظہر کی چار رکعتیں پڑھی ہیں اور اسے اس کے بیچ یا جھوٹ کہنے میں شک ہوا تو احتیاط کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ وہ نماز لوٹا لے اس لئے کہ اس کی سچائی میں جو شک ہے وہ ( دراصل ) نماز ہی میں شک ہے اور اگر امام اور مقتدیوں میں اختلاف ہوا تو اگر امام کو بالیقین یاد ہے تو وہ نماز نہ لوٹائے ورنہ ان کی بات کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے نماز لوٹالے کذافی الخلاصہ اور اگر اس نے ظہر کی نیت سے ایک رکعت پڑھی پھر اسے دوسری رکعت میں یہ شک ہوا کہ وہ عصر میں ہے پھر تیسری رکعت میں شک ہوا کہ وہ نفل پڑھ رہا ہے پھر چوتھی رکعت میں اسے شک ہوا کہ وہ ظہر میں ہے تو فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ ظہر ہی میں شمار ہوگا اور شک کا کچھا اعتبار نہیں۔ تشریح: سلام پھیرنے کے بعد کسی کو دوسرا شخص خبر دے کہ تو نے ظہر کی چار رکعت پڑھی ہے لیکن نمازی کو اس کے سچا اور جھوٹا ہونے میں شک ہے تو احتیاط اس نماز کا اعادہ کرے اس لئے کہ مخبر کی خبر میں شک گو یا نماز میں شک۔ ولو وقع الإختلاف بين الإمـام و الـقـوم: اگر امام اور مقتدیوں میں نماز کی رکعات کے بارے می اختلاف ہو جائے تو اگر امام کو اپنی بات پر پورا یقین ہے تو نماز نہ لوٹائے اور اگر یقین نہ ہو تو مقتدیوں کے کہنے کی وجہ سے نماز دو ہرائی جائے گی۔ ولو صلى ركعة بنية الظهر : اگر کسی نے ظہر کی نیت سے نماز شروع کی پھر ہر رکعت میں شک ہوتا، ہانہ نماز ظہر کی ادا ہو گی اور یہ شک اثر انداز نہ ہوگا۔
وَلَوْ تَذَكَّرَ مُصَلِى الْعَصْرِ أَنَّهُ تَرَكَ سَجْدَةً وَلَمْ يَدْرِ هَلْ تَرَكَهَا مِنَ الظَّهْرِ أَوِ الْعَصْرِ الَّذِي هُوَ فِيهَا تَحَرَّى فَإِنْ لَّمْ يَقَعُ تَحَرِّيْهِ عَلَى شَى يُتِمُّ الْعَصْرَ وَيَسْجُدُ سَجْدَةً وَاحِدَةً ثُمَّ
If no prayer has been missed so far and he wants to perform qada' umri, it is makruh. Explanation: Since certainty is not removed by doubt, and by certainty is meant definitive knowledge. Thus, from puberty, except if he has a strong presumption (zann ghalib) that some of his prayers were invalid due to missing purity or a condition, then he should make up those prayers. But if his strong presumption is that his prayers are not due, yet he still makes them up, then such qada is makruh because it is prohibited in hadith. [Arabic] Doubt in a prayer: whether he performed it or not, he repeats it within the time. Doubt in ruku' or sujud while still in it, he repeats it; if after, then no. If he doubts how many rak'at he prayed: if first time, he restarts; if frequent, he does taharri; otherwise takes the minimum. This is if doubt occurs before completion; if after, nothing is obligatory unless after completion he remembers leaving a fard and doubts its identity; they said: he performs one sajdah, then sits, then stands and prays one rak'ah with two sajdahs, then sits, then performs sajdat al-sahw. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. Urdu translation and commentary follow. [More rulings on informant after salam, imam-mamoon disagreement, doubt in intention, and a case of forgetting a sajdah during asr and doubting whether it was from zuhr or asr.]
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a detailed application of the great maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to various scenarios of doubt in prayer. The opening discussion on qada' umri illustrates that without any actual missed prayers, performing a blanket make-up is makruh because the original certainty (that all prayers were performed) is not overturned by mere possibility. The core rulings deal with specific doubts: Doubt about performing a prayer at all: if within the time, repeat; after the time, no repeat because the certainty of having performed it (or the default non-obligation) remains. Doubt about a specific action (ruku/sujud) during prayer: repeat immediately; after prayer, ignore. Doubt about the number of rak'at: if this is the first occurrence, restart; if frequent (a chronic doubter, kathir al-shakk), resort to taharri (attempt to determine the dominant opinion) and act upon it; if no dominance, take the minimum (akhdh bi'l-aqall). This is before finishing; after finishing, no obligation. Exception: after salam, if one remembers leaving a fard but cannot identify which, the remedy is: one sajdah, then sit, then stand and pray one rak'ah with two sajdahs, then sit, then perform sajdat al-sahw. Further cases: if a trustworthy person informs you after salam that you prayed four rak'at of zuhr, and you doubt his truthfulness, repeat out of precaution (ihtiyatan) because doubt in his truthfulness is doubt in the prayer itself. If imam and congregation disagree on the number of rak'at: if the imam is certain, no repeat; otherwise, repeat based on their statement. If someone starts zuhr and in each rak'at doubts whether it is asr or nafl, the prayer remains valid as zuhr because doubt in intention does not affect validity. Finally, a partial case: if an asr worshipper remembers leaving a sajdah but does not know whether it was from zuhr or asr, he should perform taharri; if that does not resolve, he completes asr and does one sajdah... (text cuts off). All these rulings demonstrate that certainty (yaqin) is the baseline, and doubt (shakk) only necessitates action when it occurs during the act itself or as a precaution to avoid leaving an obligation.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Uncertainty between two possibilities with equal probability; or doubt as opposed to certainty.
تحرّي (taharri): Effort to determine the correct or dominant opinion when in doubt, used for frequent doubters.
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precautionary measure taken to ensure an obligation is fulfilled, e.g., repeating a prayer when a trustworthy informant gives news.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person frequently doubts the number of rak'at he has prayed. He is currently in the third rak'at of Zuhr and doubts whether he prayed two or three rak'at. He has no dominant opinion. According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what should he do?
A) He should restart the prayer because it is the first occurrence.
B) He should perform taharri and act on his dominant opinion; if none, take the minimum and complete.
C) He should ignore the doubt and continue as if he has prayed three.
D) He should perform sajdat al-sahw immediately.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' governs all doubt in prayer: act on doubt only during the act, and after completion ignore unless a fard is clearly missing.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
12 min
Applying the Certainty Maxim to Prayer Doubts and Rukn Omissions
Applications of certainty maxim to prayer doubts and omissions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' to cases of doubt in prayer and omission of pillars, and identify the mufta bihi ruling for each scenario.

Core Idea
Certainty prevails over doubt, but the timing and type of omission determine whether the prayer is invalid or correctable.

The Hanafi legal maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (اليقين لا يزول بالشك) is a cornerstone of Islamic jurisprudence, especially in matters of worship where doubts frequently arise. This lesson applies the maxim to three classic scenarios in prayer: doubt during the sajdah of Fajr, forgetting a qawli or fi'li rukn after completing prayer, and forgetting qira'ah in an unknown prayer. Understanding these applications equips a mufti to issue correct fatwas when worshippers face such uncertainties.

Guided Path
1
Recall the maxim and its scope
State the maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' and explain that it means a prior certainty (e.g., having performed prayer correctly) is not overturned by subsequent doubt unless there is clear evidence. Identify that this maxim governs the rulings in the passage.
The maxim is a kubra (major) qa'idah applicable across all fiqh chapters.
2
Classify the doubt or omission
For each scenario, identify the type of uncertainty: is it doubt during the prayer (e.g., number of rak'ahs) or after completion (e.g., missing a pillar)? Also classify the omitted component as qawli (verbal) or fi'li (action).
Qawli rukn: qira'ah, takbir. Fi'li rukn: ruku, sajdah.
3
Apply the maxim to determine the ruling
Using the maxim, decide whether the doubt invalidates the prayer or allows correction. For example, doubt in second sajdah of Fajr introduces a new rak'ah, so the certainty of two rak'ahs is lost and prayer is invalid. In first sajdah, the rak'ah is not yet confirmed so the doubt is not about the number; correction is possible.
The maxim works with the specific fiqh rules about when a rak'ah is confirmed (after raising from first sajdah per Imam Muhammad).
4
Differentiate between qawli and fi'li rukn
Note that forgetting a qawli rukn (like qira'ah) invalidates the prayer permanently because it cannot be compensated after completion. Forgetting a fi'li rukn (like sajdah) is analogous to forgetting ruku and can be remedied by performing a sajdah and completing a rak'ah.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
5
Identify the mufta bihi ruling
For each scenario, determine which opinion is relied upon in fatwa. The passage cites Imam Muhammad and the Bazzaziyyah, which are later sources. Typically, the mufta bihi follows the rulings in the Bazzaziyyah as they are from the mutakhkhirin (later scholars).
The mufta bihi for the Fajr doubt in first sajdah is the allowance of correction (Imam Muhammad's view).

ترجمہ: اور اگر اس کے سجدہ میں یہ شک ہوا کہ اس نے فجر کی دور کعتیں پڑھی ہیں یا تین ؟ اگر وہ دوسرے سجدہ میں ہے تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہو گئی اور اگر وہ پہلے سجدہ میں ہے تو اس کی اصلاح ممکن ہے امام محمد کے نزدیک اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک حقیقت نماز سجدہ سہ سر اٹھانے پر پوری ہوتی ہے تو سجدہ ادھورہ چھوڑ دینے سے وہ اس طرح ختم ہو جائے گا جیسے کہ اسے حدث سے ختم کر دیا جائے تو وہ کھڑا ہو اور بیٹھ جائے اور سجدہ سہو کرے بزاز یہ میں یہ بھی فرمایا اسی مسئلہ کی طرح یہ ہے کہ اسے یاد آیا کہ اس نے کوئی قولی رکن چھوڑ دیا ہے تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی اور اگر اس نے کوئی فعلی رکن چھوڑ دیا تو رکوع چھوڑنے پر محمول کیا جائے گا تو وہ سجدہ کرے پھر بیٹھ جائے پھر کھڑا ہو اور دو سجدوں کے ساتھ ایک رکعت پڑھے۔ تشریح اگر کسی کو فجر کی نماز میں شک ہوا کہ اس نے فجر کی نماز دورکعت پڑھی ہے یا تین ؟ تو اگر یہ شک دوسرے سجدہ میں پیدا ہوا تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی کیونکہ یہاں یہ احتمال ہے کہ یہ سجدہ تیسری رکعت کا ہو اور فجر میں روہی فرض ہیں تو تیسری رکعت سے نقل شروع ہو گئے اور فرض کو پورا کرنے سے پہلے نفل شروع کر دینا دونوں کو خلط ملط کر دینا یہ موجب فساد ہے اور پہلے سجدہ میں شک ہوا تو امام محمد کے نزدیک نماز کی اصلاح ممکن ہے کیوں کہ ان کے نزدیک وہ رکعت سجدہ اولیٰ سے سر اٹھانے پر مؤکد ہوتی ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک اس رکعت کو چھوڑ دینے کی ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ اس سجدہ کو چھوڑ دے اور سجدہ کے ترک کو مؤکد کرنے کے لئے کھڑا ہو جائے پھر بیٹھ کر نماز پوری کرلے اور چونکہ قعدہ اخیرہ میں تاخیر ہو گئی اس لئے سجدہ سہو بھی کر لے یہ سجدہ چھوڑ دینے سے اس طرح ختم ہو جائے گا جیسے کہ سر اٹھانے سے پہلے حدث لاحق ہو جائے تو وہ سجدہ ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔ تذكر انه ترك ركناً قولیاً کسی شخص کو نماز سے فراغت کے بعد یاد آیا کہ اس نے رکن قولی مثلا قرآت وغیرہ چھوڑ دی تو ایسی صورت میں نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی اور نماز کے درست ہونے کی کوئی شکل نہیں ہے اور اگر کوئی رکن فعلی چھوٹ گیا ہے تو اسے ترک رکوع پر محمول کرے تو سجدہ کرے پھر بیٹھ جائے پھر کھڑے ہو کر رکوع وجود کے ساتھ ایک رکعت پوری کرکے نماز مکمل کرلے۔
صلى صَلوةَ يَوْمِ وَ لَيْلَةٍ ثُمَّ تَذَكَّرَ أَنَّهُ تَرَكَ الْقِرَاءَةَ فِي رَكْعَةٍ وَلَمْ يَعْلَمُ أَيَّةً صَلَوَةٍ أَعَادَ الْفَجْرَ وَالوِتْرَ وَ إِنْ تَذَكَّرَ أَنَّهُ تَرَكَ فِي رَكْعَتَيْنِ فَكَذَلِكَ وَ إِنْ تَذَكَّرَ الشَّرْكَ فِي الْأَرْبَعِ فَذَوَاتَ الْأَرْبَعِ كُلَّهَا إِنْتَهَى.
ترجمه: کسی نے ایک دن رات کی نمازیں پڑھیں پھر اسے یاد آیا کہ اس نے کسی رکعت میں قرآت چھوڑ دی ہے اور سیا سے یاد نہیں کہ وہ کون سی نماز بھی تو فجر اور وتر کولوٹائے اور اگر اسے یہ یاد آیا کہ اس نے دورکعتوں میں قرآت چھوڑی ہے تو بھی یہی حکم ہے اور اگر چار رکعتوں میں قرآت چھوڑنی یاد آئے تو چار والی تمام لوٹائے ۔ بزاز یہ کا کلام پورا ہوا۔
تشریح: ایک شخص نے ایک دن کی پانچوں نمازیں پڑھیں اس کے بعد یاد آیا کہ اس نے کسی نماز کی ایک رکعت میں قرآت چھوڑی ہے لیکن یہ معلوم نہیں کہ کونسی نماز تھی تو ایسی صورت میں فجر اور وتر کا اعادہ کرے اگر یاد آیا کہ دو رکعتوں میں قرآت چھوڑی ہے تو یہی حکم ہے لیکن چار رکعتوں میں ترک قرآت کے متعلق شک ہے تو پھر چاروں رکعتوں والی نمازوں کا اعادہ کرے۔
Translation: And if he doubts in his sajdah whether he has prayed the two rak'ahs of Fajr or three? If he is in the second sajdah, his prayer becomes invalid; and if he is in the first sajdah, it can be corrected according to Imam Muhammad because according to him the reality of prayer is completed upon raising the head from the sajdah. So leaving the sajdah incomplete will terminate it like terminating it by hadath. So he should stand and sit and perform sajda sahw. In Bazzaziyyah it is also stated that similar to this issue is when he remembers that he left a qawli rukn, then his prayer becomes invalid; and if he left a fi'li rukn, it will be treated like leaving ruku, so he should perform sajdah, then sit, then stand and complete one rak'ah with two sajdahs. Explanation: If someone doubts in Fajr prayer whether he has prayed two rak'ahs or three? If this doubt occurs in the second sajdah, his prayer becomes invalid because there is a possibility that this sajdah is of a third rak'ah, and in Fajr only two are fard, so a third rak'ah would be nafl, and starting nafl before completing fard and mixing them causes invalidity. If doubt occurs in the first sajdah, according to Imam Muhammad the prayer can be corrected because according to him the rak'ah is confirmed upon raising the head from the first sajdah. So one way to abandon this rak'ah is to leave this sajdah, and to confirm the abandonment of the sajdah he should stand, then sit and complete the prayer, and because of the delay in the final qa'dah he should perform sajda sahw. This sajdah will be terminated like when hadath occurs before raising the head from sajdah. Tazakkur annahu taraka ruknan qawliyyan: If after completing the prayer a person remembers that he left a qawli rukn, like qira'ah etc., then in such a case the prayer becomes invalid and there is no way to correct it. And if a fi'li rukn is left, it will be treated like leaving ruku, so he should perform sajdah, then sit, then stand and complete one rak'ah with ruku and sajdah and complete the prayer. He prayed the prayers of a day and night, then he remembered that he left qira'ah in one rak'ah and does not know which prayer, he repeats Fajr and Witr. And if he remembered that he left it in two rak'ahs, then similarly. And if he remembered sharing in four, then all four-rak'ah prayers. End. Translation: Someone prayed the five prayers of a day and night, then he remembered that he left qira'ah in one rak'ah of some prayer but does not know which prayer it was. In such a case, he repeats Fajr and Witr. If he remembered that he left qira'ah in two rak'ahs, the same ruling applies. But if he is uncertain about leaving qira'ah in four rak'ahs, then he repeats all four-rak'ah prayers.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage presents several applications of the Hanafi legal maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' to issues in prayer. The first case deals with doubt during sajdah in Fajr prayer: if the doubt about the number of rak'ahs occurs in the second sajdah, the prayer is invalid because the doubt introduces a third rak'ah which would be nafl mixed with fard. If the doubt occurs in the first sajdah, Imam Muhammad allows correction: since the rak'ah is not yet confirmed (completion of sajdah), the worshipper can abandon that incomplete rak'ah by standing and then sitting to complete the prayer, with sajda sahw for the delay. The second case: if after prayer one remembers leaving a qawli rukn (e.g., qira'ah), the prayer is invalid and cannot be fixed. If a fi'li rukn is left, it is analogized to forgetting ruku, and the remedy is to perform a sajdah, sit, then stand and complete a full rak'ah with two sajdahs. The third case: if one forgets qira'ah in a single rak'ah during a day's prayers and cannot identify which prayer, only Fajr and Witr are repeated because they are unique in rak'ah count. For two rak'ahs, the same; for four rak'ahs, all four-rak'ah prayers are repeated. Throughout, the principle is that certainty (e.g., of having completed a prayer properly) is not nullified by doubt; the minimal requirement is adhered to, and additional prayers are made up only when necessary.

Key Terms
ركن قولی (rukn qawli): A pillar of prayer that is verbal, such as qira'ah or takbir
ركن فعلی (rukn fi'li): A pillar of prayer that is an action, such as ruku or sajdah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Fajr prayer, if a person doubts whether he has prayed two or three rak'ahs while in the second sajdah, what is the ruling according to Imam Muhammad?
A) He should correct it by performing sajda sahw
B) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated
C) He should stand and add a third rak'ah
D) He should continue based on his predominant assumption

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' governs prayer omissions, but its application varies by the timing of doubt and the type of pillar omitted.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

Applying 'Certainty is not Removed by Doubt' to Divorce Doubts
Application of the certainty maxim to doubts about the occurrence and number of divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' to resolve doubts about the occurrence and number of divorces, and identify when taharri and the stricter option (ashadd) are required.

Core Idea
Certainty preserves marriage; doubt does not dissolve it. Minimum certain divorces hold unless stronger evidence or ijtihad dictates otherwise.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair demonstrates the practical force of the foundational maxim اليقين لا يزول بالشك (certainty is not removed by doubt) in family law. As a mufti, you must navigate between preserving the original marriage bond and upholding the husband's oath. Let's walk through the five scenarios to see how certainty, predominant assumption, testimony, and taharri each affect the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Classify the doubt
Determine whether the doubt is about the occurrence of talaq itself or about the number (one, two, or three). The ruling differs fundamentally.
Doubt about occurrence: no talaq. Doubt about number: minimum certain is applied.
2
Apply the maxim to the minimum
If the occurrence is certain but the number is doubtful, the minimum (one) is taken because that is the certain amount. Additional numbers are not certain.
Exceptions: if the husband is certain of more, or has predominant assumption (ghalabah al-zann) of more, that overrides the minimum.
3
Evaluate testimony and confession
If reliable witnesses testify to one divorce and the husband believes them, accept their testimony. If the husband himself confesses certainty of three, that is binding.
Testimony requires reliability (adalah). The husband's own certainty is a confession.
4
Handle the oath-and-forget scenario
If the husband swore by talaq but cannot recall the number, he must perform taharri (personal ijtihad) to determine the most likely number. If equal, take the stricter (ashadd) – the option most harmful to him.
This is the view of Imam Abu Yusuf as recorded in al-Bazzaziyyah, and it is the mufta bihi position.
5
Synthesize the fatwa process
The mufti must ask: Is the occurrence certain? If no, no talaq. If yes, what is the number? Use certainty, predominant assumption, testimony, confession, or taharri/ashadd in that order.
Always prioritize what is certain over doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و منها شك هل طلق أم لا لم يقع شك أن طلق واحدة أو أكثر بنى على الأقل كما ذكره الإسجابي إلا أن يستيقن بالأكثر أو يكون أكبر ظنه على خلافه و إن قال الزوج عزمت على أنه ثلاث يتركها و إن أخبر عدول حضروا ذلك المجلس بأنها واحدة و صدقهم أخذ بقولهم إن كانوا عدولا و عن الإمام الثاني حلف بطلاقها و لا يدري أثلاث أم أقل يتحرى و إن استويا عمل بأشد ذلك عليه كذا في البزازية. ترجمه اور اسی کی ایک صورت ہے کہ شک ہوا کہ طلاق دی ہے یا نہیں تو واقع نہیں ہوگی شک ہوا کہ ایک طلاق دی ہے یا زیادہ؟ تو اقل پر محمول کیا جائے گا علامہ اسیجائی نے ایسا ہی لکھا ہے الا یہ کہ اکثر کا یقین ہو یا اس کا غالب گمان اس (اقل) کے برخلاف ہو اور اگر شوہر کہے کہ مجھے تین طلاق کا یقین ہے تو اسے ( بیوی کو ) چھوڑ دے اور اگر اسے اس مجلس میں موجود عادل لوگوں نے خبر دی کہ طلاق ایک ہی تھی اور وہ انہیں سچا جانے تو وہ ان کے قول کو اختیار کر لے شرط یہ ہے کہ وہ عادل ہوں اور امام یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ شوہر نے بیوی کو طلاق دینے پر قسم کھائی لیکن اسے یہ معلوم نہیں کہ وہ تین تھیں یا ان سے کم ؟ تو وہ تحری کرے اور اگر دونوں جانب برابر ہوں تو اس پر جو اشد ہو اس پر عمل کرے بزاز یہ میں اسی طرح ہے۔ تشریح: ایک شخص کو شک ہوا کہ اس نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق دی ہے یا نہیں ؟ تو ایسی صورت میں وقوع طلاق کا حکم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ بقاء نکاح اصل چیز ہے لہذا محض شک کی وجہ سے اصل چیز ختم نہ ہوگی. و منها شك انه طلق واحدة او اكثر : اگر طلاق دینے کا تو یقین ہے لیکن ایک دی یا دو یا تین ؟ اس میں شک ہے تو چونکہ نکاح بالیقین ہے اور اسے ختم کرنے والی ایک طلاق بھی بالیقین ہے اس لئے ایک کا حکم لگ یا جائے گا اور دو یا تین کا شک ہے اس لئے صرف شک کی صورت میں دو یا تین طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی ہاں اگر دو یا تین کا یقین ہو یا ظن غالب تو گمان کے مطابق فیصلہ کیا جائے گا نیز اگر شوہر خود ہی تین کے یقین کا اقرار کرے تو بھی تین ہی واقع ہوگی تو بیوی کو فوراً چھوڑے اور علیحدگی واجب ہے. و إن أخبره عدول : اگر بوقت طلاق کچھ عادل لوگ موجود ہوں اور وہ عادل ایک طلاق دینے کی بات کہیں اور شوہر کو لگے کہ یہ بیچ بول رہے ہیں تو ایک ہی طلاق مانی جائے گی ، لیکن امام یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ تحری کرکے اس
And among them: doubt whether he divorced or not - it does not occur. Doubt whether he divorced one or more - he builds on the minimum as mentioned by al-Isjabi, unless he is certain of the greater or his predominant assumption is contrary. And if the husband says 'I am certain that it is three', he leaves her. And if reliable persons who were present at that gathering inform him that it was one and he believes them, he accepts their statement provided they are reliable. And it is narrated from Imam al-Thani (Abu Yusuf) that he swore by her divorce and does not know whether three or less - he performs taharri, and if they are equal, he acts upon the severer of them. Thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. Translation: And one of its cases is that if he doubts whether he gave divorce, it does not occur. If he doubts whether he gave one divorce or more, it will be construed as the minimum, as Allamah Isjabi wrote, unless he is certain of the greater or his predominant assumption is contrary. And if the husband says 'I am certain that it is three', then he leaves her. And if reliable persons who were present in that gathering inform him that it was one and he believes them, he accepts their statement, provided they are reliable. And it is narrated from Imam Yusuf that the husband swore by her divorce and he does not know whether three or less, he performs taharri, and if both sides are equal, he acts upon the severer of them. Thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. Explanation: A person doubts whether he divorced his wife or not? In such a case, the occurrence of divorce is not ruled because the continuance of marriage is the original matter, so mere doubt does not nullify the original. And from them: doubt whether he divorced one or more: If he is certain that he gave divorce but doubts whether one, two, or three, then because marriage is certain and one divorce is also certain to have occurred, the ruling of one is applied. Two or three are doubted, so mere doubt does not cause two or three divorces to occur. Yes, if he is certain of two or three or has predominant assumption, he decides according to his assumption. Also, if the husband himself confesses certainty of three, then three occur, and he must immediately leave her and separation is obligatory. And if reliable persons inform him: If at the time of divorce some reliable persons were present and they say that one divorce occurred, and the husband thinks they are telling the truth, then one divorce is accepted. However, Imam Yusuf says that he should perform taharri and...
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage applies the maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' to cases of talaq. The text presents several scenarios. First, if a person doubts whether he even uttered a divorce, no divorce occurs because the original state (marriage) remains. Second, if he is certain a divorce occurred but doubts the number (one, two, or three), the minimum (one) is taken based on certainty. Exceptions: if he is certain of more, or his predominant assumption (ghalabah al-zann) supports more, then that number applies. Third, if the husband himself says he is certain it was three, it is treated as three and he must separate immediately. Fourth, if reliable witnesses testify that it was one, their testimony is accepted. Finally, Imam Abu Yusuf's view: if the husband swears by divorce and cannot recall the number, he should exert ijtihad (taharri); if possibilities are equal, he must take the stricter option (most harm to him). This reflects the Hanafi principle that in matters of uncertainty, the original state (marriage) continues unless certainty or strong presumption establishes otherwise.

Key Terms
تحری (taharri): A personal ijtihad or effort to determine the most likely number of divorces when uncertain
یشد (ashadd): The stricter or more severe option (in terms of consequences for the husband)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband is certain he uttered a divorce but doubts whether it was one or two. What is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) No divorce occurs because of the doubt
B) Two divorces occur because that is the safer option
C) One divorce occurs, because it is the minimum certain
D) He must reconcile with his wife and repeat the divorce

Key Takeaway
When doubt arises in talaq, certainty prevails: no divorce if occurrence is doubted, one divorce if number is doubted, unless stronger evidence or ijtihad dictates otherwise.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
8 min
Certainty is Not Removed by Doubt: Oaths and Purity
Explaining the maxim with two furuat and an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' to cases of doubt in divorce oaths and post-sleep emissions, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute with its mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Certainty governs; in doubt, act on the lesser if it is a matter of obligation, but precaution may require the greater.

The great maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (Certainty is not removed by doubt) is a cornerstone of Hanafi fatwa. In this passage, Ibn Nujaym applies it to two concrete scenarios: doubt over the number of divorce oaths, and doubt over the nature of a discharge after sleep. Both illustrate how the principle works, and the second reveals a healthy ikhtilaf within the school. Understanding these furuat will sharpen your ability to use this maxim in real fatwa work.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its core implication
The maxim means that once certainty is established, it persists until a new certainty overrides it. Doubt (shakk) cannot remove it. In fiqh, this usually means acting on the lesser when the doubt is about the extent of an obligation.
The lesser is certain; the greater is doubtful.
2
Analyze the first furu': doubt in divorce oaths
If a man doubts whether he swore one divorce or less, he acts on the one (the lesser) because it is certain. If he is certain of three, then three are enforced. This is direct application: the certain number is binding.
If he remembers three clearly, that new certainty overrides the doubt.
3
Analyze the second furu': doubt about mani or madhi after sleep
If after sleep one finds moisture and doubts whether it is mani (requires ghusl) or madhi (only wudu), the ruling depends on recollection of a wet dream. If the dream is remembered, ghusl is wajib by consensus. If not, Abu Yusuf holds no ghusl (acting on the lesser), while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require ghusl out of precaution. The text states the fatwa is on the precautionary view.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The precautionary view is mufta bihi.
4
Understand the analogies given
Two analogies support the precautionary position: (a) direct touching of private parts (mubashara fahisha) nullifies wudu according to the two shaykhs; (b) if a dead mouse is found in a well and the time of fall is unknown, Imam Abu Hanifa rules based on decomposition, but the two companions consider the well impure from the time of discovery. Both show ihtiyat (precaution) in doubtful matters.
These analogies strengthen the case for obligating ghusl.
5
Determine the mufta bihi for each case
For divorce oaths: act on the certain number. For post-sleep emission: if no dream is remembered, ghusl is wajib (Shaykhayn's view) as per the fatwa. The maxim is applied but with precaution dominating.
This teaches that ihtiyat can override the 'lesser is certain' rule when obligation is at stake.
