كے مطابق عمل کرے اور اگر تحری کے بعد دونوں جانب برابر ہوں تو اشد پر عمل کرے امام یوسف کا قول احتیاط پر مبنی ہے قیاس وضابطہ پونی ہیں اس پر عمل کرنا بہتر ہے لیکن دوسرے کو فتوی دینے یا فیصلہ کرنے میں ضابطہ ہی کو اختیار کیا جائے گا۔ حلف بطلاقها : ایک شخص کو شک ہوا کہ اس نے ایک طلاق کی قسم کھائی تھی یا اس سے کم کی تو ایسی صورت میں اقل چونکہ یقینی ہے لہذا اس پر مدار ہو گا ہاں اگر زیادہ کا یقین ہو تو پھر زیادہ پر محمول کیا جائے گا اور اگر شوہر کہے کہ مجھے اچھی طرح یاد ہے کہ میں نے تین کی قسم کھائی تھی تو پھر عورت کو علیحدہ کر دیا جائے گا۔
وَمِنْهَا شَكَّ فِي الْخَارِجِ أَمَنِيٌّ أَوْ مَدِيٌّ وَكَانَ فِي النَّوْمِ فَإِنْ تَذَكَّرَ إِحْتِلَامًا وَجَبَ الْغُسْلُ إتّفَاقًا وَ إِلَّا لَمْ يَجِبْ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ عَمَلًا بِالأَقَلَّ وَهُوَ الْمَذِيُّ وَوَجَبَ عِنْدَهُمَا إحْتِيَاطًا كَقَوْلِهِمَا بِالنَّقْضِ بِالْمُبَاشَرَةِ الْفَاحِشَةِ وَكَقَوْلِ الإِمَامِ فِي الْفَارَةِ الْمَيْتَةِ إِذَا وجدَتْ فِي بِشْرٍ وَلَمْ يُدْرَ مَتى وَقَعَتْ .
ترجمہ اور اس کا جزئیہ ہے کہ اگر نکلنے والی چیز میں شک ہو کہ رومنی ہے یا ندی؟ اور وہ سو کر اٹھا ہو تو اگر اسے حتلام یاد ہو تو بالاتفاق غسل واجب ہے ورنہ تو امام یوسف کے نزدیک اقل یعنی بدی پر محمول کرتے ہوئے غسل واجب نہیں اور طرفین کے نزدیک احتیاطا غسل واجب ہے جیسا کہ وہ مباشرت فاحشہ میں نقض وضو کے قائل ہیں اور جیسا کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس مری ہوئی چوہیا کے بارے میں فرماتے ہیں جو کنویں میں پائی گئی اور یہ معلوم نہ ہو کہ وہ کب گری ہے۔ تشریح کسی شخص کو شرمگاہ سے نکلنے والی تری کے بارے میں شک ہوا کہ ندی ہے یا منی ؟ لہذا اگر احتلام یاد ہوتو بالاتفاق عسل واجب ہے اور اگر احتلام یاد نہ ہو تو امام یوسف کے نزدیک اقل یعنی ندی پر عمل کرتے ہوئے نسل کو واجب قرار نہیں دیا جائے گا جبکہ شیخین کے نزدیک احتیاطا غسل واجب ہوگا اس قول پر فتوی ہے۔ كقولها بالنقض بالمباشرة : مباشرت فاحشہ یعنی بلا کسی رکاوٹ اور حائل کے شرمگاہ سے شرمگاہ ملا نا خواہ مرد کا عورت سے ہو یا مرد کا مرد سے با عورت کا عورت سے اس سے حضرات شیخین کے نزدیک وضوٹوٹ جائے گا۔ و كقول الامام في الفارة الميتة: کنویں میں مری ہوئی چوہیا پائی گئی اور اس کنویں سے وضو کر کے نماز پڑھی گئی تو ایسی صورت میں امام صاحب کے نزدیک اگر وہ پھول کر پھٹ گئی ہو تو تین دن کی نماز لوٹائی جائے گی اور اگر پھولی پھٹی نہ ہو تو ایک دن ایک رات کی نمازوں کا اعادہ ہو گا۔ جبکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک جب سے علم ہوا ہے اس وقت سے کنواں ناپاک شمار ہوگا۔ ضابطہ ہے الیقین لا يرتفع الا باليقين - اليقين لا يزول بالشک ۔
وَهَهُنَا فُرُوْعٌ لَمْ أَرَهَا الآنَ الأَوَّلُ لَوْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ دِيْنٌ وَ شَكٍّ فِي قَدْرِهِ يَنْبَغِي لُزُوْمُ إِخْرَاجِ الْقَدْرِ الْمُتَيَقْنِ وَ فِي الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ مِنَ الْقَضَاءِ إِذَا شَكَ فِيْمَا يُدْعَى عَلَيْهِ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُرْضِى خَصْمَةً وَ لَا يَحْلِفَ إِحْتِرَارًا عَنِ الْوُقُوْعِ فِي الْحَرَامِ وَ إِنْ أَبِي خَصْمُهُ إِلَّا خَلْفَهُ إِنْ كَانَ أَكْبَرُ رَأْيِهِ أَنَّ الْمُدَّعِي مُحِقِّ لَا يَحْلِفُ وَ إِنْ كَانَ أَكْبَرُ رَأْيِهِ أَنَّهُ مُبْطِلٌ سَاعَ لَهُ الْخَلْفُ إِنْتَهَى. الثَّانِي لَهُ إِبِلٌ وَ بَقَرٌ وَ غَنَمَ وَسَائِمَةً وَ شَكٍّ فِي أَنَّ عَلَيْهِ زَكَوةَ كُلَّهَا أَوْ بَعْضِهَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ تَلْزَمَهُ زَكَوةَ الكُلِّ الثَّالِثُ شَكٍّ فِيْمَا عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّابِعُ شَكَّتْ فِيْمَا عَلَيْهَا مِنَ الْعِدَّةِ هَلْ هِيَ عِدَّةُ طَلَاقِ أَوْ وَفَاةِ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُلْزَمَ الْأَكْثَرُ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى الصَّائِمِ أَخْذَا مِنْ قَوْلِهِمْ لَوْ تَرَكَ صَلوةٌ وَ شَكٍّ أَنَّهَا أَيَّةً صَلوَةٍ تَلْزَمُهُ صَلوةُ يَوْمٍ وَ لَيْلَةٍ عَمَلًا بِالاحْتِيَاطِ ترجمه: دوسرا جزئیہ کسی کے پاس کچھ سائمہ اونٹ کچھ گائیں اور کچھ بکریاں ہیں اور اسے شک ہوا کہ اسلام ان تمام کی زکاۃ ہے یا کچھ کی واجب ہے تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس پر تمام کی زکاۃ واجب ہو۔ تیسرا جزئیہ شک ہوا کہ آیا کے ذمہ کتنے روزے ہیں۔ چوتھا جزئیہ معدہ کو شک ہوا کہ اس پر کون سی عدہ ہے عدت طلاق یا عدت وبات
He should act according to [the principle], and if after deliberation both sides are equal, then he should act on the stricter. Imam Yusuf's statement is based on precaution; analogy and principle are [clear], it is better to act on it, but for giving fatwa or judgment to another, only the principle will be adopted. Oath of divorce: A person doubts whether he swore an oath of one divorce or less, then in such a case, the lesser is certain, so it will be considered. Yes, if there is certainty of more, then it will be carried on the more. And if the husband says, 'I clearly remember that I swore three,' then the woman will be separated. Among them: doubt about the discharge whether it is mani or madhi, and he was in sleep, then if he remembers a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory by agreement; otherwise, according to Abu Yusuf, it is not obligatory, acting on the lesser, which is madhi; and according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is obligatory out of precaution, like their ruling on nullification by excessive touching, and like the Imam's statement about the dead mouse found in a well and it is not known when it fell. Translation and its branch: If there is doubt about the discharged substance whether it is mani or madhi, and he woke up from sleep, then if he remembers a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory by consensus. Otherwise, according to Imam Yusuf, acting on the lesser, i.e., madhi, ghusl is not obligatory. And according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), out of precaution, ghusl is obligatory, just as they hold that wudu is nullified by excessive touching, and as the Imam says about the dead mouse found in a well and it is not known when it fell. Explanation: A person doubts about moisture coming from the private part whether it is madhi or mani. So if he remembers a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory by consensus. If he does not remember a wet dream, then according to Imam Yusuf, acting on the lesser, i.e., madhi, ghusl will not be deemed obligatory. According to the two shaykhs, out of precaution, ghusl will be obligatory; this is the fatwa. Like their statement on nullification by excessive touching: excessive touching means contacting private parts without any barrier, whether male with female, male with male, or female with female; according to the two shaykhs, wudu is broken. And like the Imam's statement about the dead mouse: a dead mouse is found in a well and wudu and prayer have been performed with that well. In such a case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if it has swelled and burst, then three days' prayers are repeated; if it has not swelled and burst, then one day and one night's prayers are repeated. According to the two companions, from the time it became known, the well is considered impure. The rule is: Certainty is only removed by certainty; certainty is not removed by doubt. And here there are branches that I have not seen now: First: If he owes a debt and doubts its amount, it is appropriate to require paying the certain amount. And in al-Bazzaziyya from the chapter of qada: if he doubts what is claimed against him, he should satisfy his opponent and not take an oath, guarding against falling into the forbidden. And if his opponent insists on making him swear, then if his predominant opinion is that the claimant is truthful, he should not swear; if his predominant opinion is that he is false, then it is permissible for him to swear. End. Second: He has camels, cows, and goats as grazing livestock, and he doubts whether zakat is due on all or part of them, it is appropriate that zakat on all be obligatory. Third: Doubt about what is due of fasting. Fourth: A woman doubts about her iddah, whether it is iddah of divorce or death, it is appropriate that the greater be imposed on her. And on the fasting person, taking from their statement: if he left a prayer and doubts which prayer it was, then a day and night's prayer is obligatory as a precaution. Translation: Second branch: Someone has some grazing camels, some cows, and some goats, and he doubts whether zakat on all or some is obligatory, then it is appropriate that zakat on all be obligatory. Third branch: He doubts how many fasts are due. Fourth branch: A woman doubts what iddah she is in, iddah of divorce or iddah of death.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the foundational Hanafi maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (Certainty is not removed by doubt). The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains its application across several fiqh chapters. The discussion begins with oaths of divorce: if a man doubts whether he swore one divorce or less, he acts on the lesser (one) because that is certain. If he is certain of three, then three apply. Next is a purity issue: after sleep, if one finds moisture and doubts whether it is mani (requiring ghusl) or madhi (only wudu), the rule is: if a wet dream is remembered, ghusl is obligatory by consensus; otherwise, Imam Abu Yusuf says no ghusl (acting on the lesser = madhi), while the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) require ghusl out of precaution. The author notes that the fatwa is on the precautionary view. Two analogies are given: (a) wudu is broken by direct touching of private parts (according to the two shaykhs), and (b) if a dead mouse is found in a well, Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling depends on whether it had decomposed (three days' prayers repeated) or not (one day), while the two companions consider the well impure from the time of discovery. The maxim is then stated. After that, four new branches are presented applying the same principle: (1) debt: if the amount is doubtful, pay the certain minimum; (2) zakat on mixed livestock: if one doubts whether all or some are subject to zakat, all are calculated; (3) fasting: if the number of fasts is forgotten, one must estimate; (4) iddah: if a woman doubts whether her iddah is for divorce or death, the longer period applies. The passage also advises a defendant in court: if doubtful about a claim, avoid swearing and try to settle; only if the claimant insists may the defendant swear if he believes the claimant is false. The overall lesson is that certainty governs, and in doubt one either takes the lesser (if it's a matter of obligation) or the greater (if it's a matter of precaution), depending on the context.

Key Terms
اليقين (al-yaqeen): Absolute certainty that is not shaken by doubt
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt where both possibilities are equally strong
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Legal precaution; acting on the stricter side in case of doubt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fatwa, what is the ruling for a person who finds moisture after sleep without remembering a dream?
A) Ghusl is not required because the doubt does not remove certainty of purity.
B) Ghusl is required out of precaution, and this is the mufta bihi.
C) Ghusl is required only if he remembers a dream.
D) It is optional; he may choose.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' is fundamental, but in cases involving potential ritual impurity, the Hanafi school often adopts precaution (ihtiyat) as mufta bihi.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
8 min
Certainty in Debt, Zakat, Fasting, and Iddah
Applying the maxim to debt, zakat, fasting, and iddah with practical guidance for judges.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' to cases of doubt in debt amounts, mixed livestock zakat, number of fasts, and type of iddah, and explain when the greater is taken.

Core Idea
In financial obligations, pay the certain minimum; in ritual obligations with multiple types, the entire category becomes subject to zakat or the longer period is imposed as precaution.

Ibn Nujaym continues to demonstrate the far-reaching application of the maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' across four more fiqh chapters: debt, zakat, fasting, and iddah. Here, the principle sometimes dictates taking the lesser (debt) and sometimes the greater (zakat, iddah). Understanding this nuance is crucial for a mufti. The passage also includes a practical tip for judges about swearing oaths.

Guided Path
1
Review the maxim and the 'lesser vs greater' distinction
The maxim preserves certainty. When uncertain about the amount of an obligation, the certain minimum is binding. But when the doubt is about the very type of obligation (e.g., which iddah or which zakat category), the precautionary approach may impose the greater.
The key is: what is the certain element?
2
Analyze the debt furu'
If a person owes a debt but is unsure of the exact amount, he must pay the amount he is certain of (the minimum). This is direct application of the maxim: the certain amount is obligatory. The text also adds a court etiquette: if a defendant doubts the claim, he should try to settle and avoid swearing; if compelled, he may swear only if his predominant opinion is that the plaintiff is false.
This shows that the maxim also guides procedural ethics.
3
Analyze the zakat furu'
If a person has grazing camels, cows, and goats (mixed livestock) and doubts whether zakat is due on all or some, the ruling is that zakat on all is obligatory. Why? Because the entire category is subject to zakat; the doubt is not about the liability of the category but about the number of animals. Since all are potentially subject, the precaution is to pay zakat on all.
This is a case where 'acting on the greater' comes from the nature of the obligation.
4
Analyze the fasting furu'
If a person doubts the number of fasts he owes (e.g., from missed Ramadan), he must determine the certain number. The text does not elaborate, but the principle is to act on the certain minimum. However, the analogy with missed prayer (a day and night's prayer) suggests precaution.
Here the maxim may lead to estimating the minimum, but the text hints at ihtiyat.
5
Analyze the iddah furu'
If a woman doubts whether she is in iddah of divorce (3 months) or death (4 months 10 days), the greater period (4 months 10 days) is imposed. This is precaution: because the doubt is about the type of obligation, and the longer period ensures the obligation is fulfilled completely.
This is opposite to the debt case; here the greater is taken due to the nature of the duty.

كے مطابق عمل کرے اور اگر تحری کے بعد دونوں جانب برابر ہوں تو اشد پر عمل کرے امام یوسف کا قول احتیاط پر مبنی ہے قیاس وضابطہ پونی ہیں اس پر عمل کرنا بہتر ہے لیکن دوسرے کو فتوی دینے یا فیصلہ کرنے میں ضابطہ ہی کو اختیار کیا جائے گا۔ حلف بطلاقها : ایک شخص کو شک ہوا کہ اس نے ایک طلاق کی قسم کھائی تھی یا اس سے کم کی تو ایسی صورت میں اقل چونکہ یقینی ہے لہذا اس پر مدار ہو گا ہاں اگر زیادہ کا یقین ہو تو پھر زیادہ پر محمول کیا جائے گا اور اگر شوہر کہے کہ مجھے اچھی طرح یاد ہے کہ میں نے تین کی قسم کھائی تھی تو پھر عورت کو علیحدہ کر دیا جائے گا۔
وَمِنْهَا شَكَّ فِي الْخَارِجِ أَمَنِيٌّ أَوْ مَدِيٌّ وَكَانَ فِي النَّوْمِ فَإِنْ تَذَكَّرَ إِحْتِلَامًا وَجَبَ الْغُسْلُ إتّفَاقًا وَ إِلَّا لَمْ يَجِبْ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ عَمَلًا بِالأَقَلَّ وَهُوَ الْمَذِيُّ وَوَجَبَ عِنْدَهُمَا إحْتِيَاطًا كَقَوْلِهِمَا بِالنَّقْضِ بِالْمُبَاشَرَةِ الْفَاحِشَةِ وَكَقَوْلِ الإِمَامِ فِي الْفَارَةِ الْمَيْتَةِ إِذَا وجدَتْ فِي بِشْرٍ وَلَمْ يُدْرَ مَتى وَقَعَتْ .
ترجمہ اور اس کا جزئیہ ہے کہ اگر نکلنے والی چیز میں شک ہو کہ رومنی ہے یا ندی؟ اور وہ سو کر اٹھا ہو تو اگر اسے حتلام یاد ہو تو بالاتفاق غسل واجب ہے ورنہ تو امام یوسف کے نزدیک اقل یعنی بدی پر محمول کرتے ہوئے غسل واجب نہیں اور طرفین کے نزدیک احتیاطا غسل واجب ہے جیسا کہ وہ مباشرت فاحشہ میں نقض وضو کے قائل ہیں اور جیسا کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس مری ہوئی چوہیا کے بارے میں فرماتے ہیں جو کنویں میں پائی گئی اور یہ معلوم نہ ہو کہ وہ کب گری ہے۔ تشریح کسی شخص کو شرمگاہ سے نکلنے والی تری کے بارے میں شک ہوا کہ ندی ہے یا منی ؟ لہذا اگر احتلام یاد ہوتو بالاتفاق عسل واجب ہے اور اگر احتلام یاد نہ ہو تو امام یوسف کے نزدیک اقل یعنی ندی پر عمل کرتے ہوئے نسل کو واجب قرار نہیں دیا جائے گا جبکہ شیخین کے نزدیک احتیاطا غسل واجب ہوگا اس قول پر فتوی ہے۔ كقولها بالنقض بالمباشرة : مباشرت فاحشہ یعنی بلا کسی رکاوٹ اور حائل کے شرمگاہ سے شرمگاہ ملا نا خواہ مرد کا عورت سے ہو یا مرد کا مرد سے با عورت کا عورت سے اس سے حضرات شیخین کے نزدیک وضوٹوٹ جائے گا۔ و كقول الامام في الفارة الميتة: کنویں میں مری ہوئی چوہیا پائی گئی اور اس کنویں سے وضو کر کے نماز پڑھی گئی تو ایسی صورت میں امام صاحب کے نزدیک اگر وہ پھول کر پھٹ گئی ہو تو تین دن کی نماز لوٹائی جائے گی اور اگر پھولی پھٹی نہ ہو تو ایک دن ایک رات کی نمازوں کا اعادہ ہو گا۔ جبکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک جب سے علم ہوا ہے اس وقت سے کنواں ناپاک شمار ہوگا۔ ضابطہ ہے الیقین لا يرتفع الا باليقين - اليقين لا يزول بالشک ۔
وَهَهُنَا فُرُوْعٌ لَمْ أَرَهَا الآنَ الأَوَّلُ لَوْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ دِيْنٌ وَ شَكٍّ فِي قَدْرِهِ يَنْبَغِي لُزُوْمُ إِخْرَاجِ الْقَدْرِ الْمُتَيَقْنِ وَ فِي الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ مِنَ الْقَضَاءِ إِذَا شَكَ فِيْمَا يُدْعَى عَلَيْهِ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُرْضِى خَصْمَةً وَ لَا يَحْلِفَ إِحْتِرَارًا عَنِ الْوُقُوْعِ فِي الْحَرَامِ وَ إِنْ أَبِي خَصْمُهُ إِلَّا خَلْفَهُ إِنْ كَانَ أَكْبَرُ رَأْيِهِ أَنَّ الْمُدَّعِي مُحِقِّ لَا يَحْلِفُ وَ إِنْ كَانَ أَكْبَرُ رَأْيِهِ أَنَّهُ مُبْطِلٌ سَاعَ لَهُ الْخَلْفُ إِنْتَهَى. الثَّانِي لَهُ إِبِلٌ وَ بَقَرٌ وَ غَنَمَ وَسَائِمَةً وَ شَكٍّ فِي أَنَّ عَلَيْهِ زَكَوةَ كُلَّهَا أَوْ بَعْضِهَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ تَلْزَمَهُ زَكَوةَ الكُلِّ الثَّالِثُ شَكٍّ فِيْمَا عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّابِعُ شَكَّتْ فِيْمَا عَلَيْهَا مِنَ الْعِدَّةِ هَلْ هِيَ عِدَّةُ طَلَاقِ أَوْ وَفَاةِ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُلْزَمَ الْأَكْثَرُ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى الصَّائِمِ أَخْذَا مِنْ قَوْلِهِمْ لَوْ تَرَكَ صَلوةٌ وَ شَكٍّ أَنَّهَا أَيَّةً صَلوَةٍ تَلْزَمُهُ صَلوةُ يَوْمٍ وَ لَيْلَةٍ عَمَلًا بِالاحْتِيَاطِ ترجمه: دوسرا جزئیہ کسی کے پاس کچھ سائمہ اونٹ کچھ گائیں اور کچھ بکریاں ہیں اور اسے شک ہوا کہ اسلام ان تمام کی زکاۃ ہے یا کچھ کی واجب ہے تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس پر تمام کی زکاۃ واجب ہو۔ تیسرا جزئیہ شک ہوا کہ آیا کے ذمہ کتنے روزے ہیں۔ چوتھا جزئیہ معدہ کو شک ہوا کہ اس پر کون سی عدہ ہے عدت طلاق یا عدت وبات
He should act according to [the principle], and if after deliberation both sides are equal, then he should act on the stricter. Imam Yusuf's statement is based on precaution; analogy and principle are [clear], it is better to act on it, but for giving fatwa or judgment to another, only the principle will be adopted. Oath of divorce: A person doubts whether he swore an oath of one divorce or less, then in such a case, the lesser is certain, so it will be considered. Yes, if there is certainty of more, then it will be carried on the more. And if the husband says, 'I clearly remember that I swore three,' then the woman will be separated. Among them: doubt about the discharge whether it is mani or madhi, and he was in sleep, then if he remembers a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory by agreement; otherwise, according to Abu Yusuf, it is not obligatory, acting on the lesser, which is madhi; and according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is obligatory out of precaution, like their ruling on nullification by excessive touching, and like the Imam's statement about the dead mouse found in a well and it is not known when it fell. Translation and its branch: If there is doubt about the discharged substance whether it is mani or madhi, and he woke up from sleep, then if he remembers a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory by consensus. Otherwise, according to Imam Yusuf, acting on the lesser, i.e., madhi, ghusl is not obligatory. And according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), out of precaution, ghusl is obligatory, just as they hold that wudu is nullified by excessive touching, and as the Imam says about the dead mouse found in a well and it is not known when it fell. Explanation: A person doubts about moisture coming from the private part whether it is madhi or mani. So if he remembers a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory by consensus. If he does not remember a wet dream, then according to Imam Yusuf, acting on the lesser, i.e., madhi, ghusl will not be deemed obligatory. According to the two shaykhs, out of precaution, ghusl will be obligatory; this is the fatwa. Like their statement on nullification by excessive touching: excessive touching means contacting private parts without any barrier, whether male with female, male with male, or female with female; according to the two shaykhs, wudu is broken. And like the Imam's statement about the dead mouse: a dead mouse is found in a well and wudu and prayer have been performed with that well. In such a case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if it has swelled and burst, then three days' prayers are repeated; if it has not swelled and burst, then one day and one night's prayers are repeated. According to the two companions, from the time it became known, the well is considered impure. The rule is: Certainty is only removed by certainty; certainty is not removed by doubt. And here there are branches that I have not seen now: First: If he owes a debt and doubts its amount, it is appropriate to require paying the certain amount. And in al-Bazzaziyya from the chapter of qada: if he doubts what is claimed against him, he should satisfy his opponent and not take an oath, guarding against falling into the forbidden. And if his opponent insists on making him swear, then if his predominant opinion is that the claimant is truthful, he should not swear; if his predominant opinion is that he is false, then it is permissible for him to swear. End. Second: He has camels, cows, and goats as grazing livestock, and he doubts whether zakat is due on all or part of them, it is appropriate that zakat on all be obligatory. Third: Doubt about what is due of fasting. Fourth: A woman doubts about her iddah, whether it is iddah of divorce or death, it is appropriate that the greater be imposed on her. And on the fasting person, taking from their statement: if he left a prayer and doubts which prayer it was, then a day and night's prayer is obligatory as a precaution. Translation: Second branch: Someone has some grazing camels, some cows, and some goats, and he doubts whether zakat on all or some is obligatory, then it is appropriate that zakat on all be obligatory. Third branch: He doubts how many fasts are due. Fourth branch: A woman doubts what iddah she is in, iddah of divorce or iddah of death.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the foundational Hanafi maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (Certainty is not removed by doubt). The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains its application across several fiqh chapters. The discussion begins with oaths of divorce: if a man doubts whether he swore one divorce or less, he acts on the lesser (one) because that is certain. If he is certain of three, then three apply. Next is a purity issue: after sleep, if one finds moisture and doubts whether it is mani (requiring ghusl) or madhi (only wudu), the rule is: if a wet dream is remembered, ghusl is obligatory by consensus; otherwise, Imam Abu Yusuf says no ghusl (acting on the lesser = madhi), while the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) require ghusl out of precaution. The author notes that the fatwa is on the precautionary view. Two analogies are given: (a) wudu is broken by direct touching of private parts (according to the two shaykhs), and (b) if a dead mouse is found in a well, Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling depends on whether it had decomposed (three days' prayers repeated) or not (one day), while the two companions consider the well impure from the time of discovery. The maxim is then stated. After that, four new branches are presented applying the same principle: (1) debt: if the amount is doubtful, pay the certain minimum; (2) zakat on mixed livestock: if one doubts whether all or some are subject to zakat, all are calculated; (3) fasting: if the number of fasts is forgotten, one must estimate; (4) iddah: if a woman doubts whether her iddah is for divorce or death, the longer period applies. The passage also advises a defendant in court: if doubtful about a claim, avoid swearing and try to settle; only if the claimant insists may the defendant swear if he believes the claimant is false. The overall lesson is that certainty governs, and in doubt one either takes the lesser (if it's a matter of obligation) or the greater (if it's a matter of precaution), depending on the context.

Key Terms
اليقين (al-yaqeen): Absolute certainty that is not shaken by doubt
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt where both possibilities are equally strong
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Legal precaution; acting on the stricter side in case of doubt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person doubts the amount of debt he owes, what should he do?
A) Pay the maximum possible amount to be safe.
B) Pay only the amount he is certain of.
C) Pay nothing until the exact amount is known.
D) Consult a scholar and pay whatever they suggest.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' is applied consistently across different fiqh chapters, but the outcome (lesser vs greater) depends on whether the doubt is about quantity or type of obligation.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
12 min
Applying Caution (Ihtiyat) in Doubtful Worship and Oaths
Illustrates the principle of caution with six furuat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi qawida that when doubt arises about the type or quantity of an obligation, one should act on the greater (akthar) as a precaution (ihtiyat).

Core Idea
In doubt about an obligation's type or quantity, caution requires acting on the greater to ensure fulfillment.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents a key qawida: when uncertainty exists about the exact obligation, one should take the more cautious path by performing the greater possible obligation. The author illustrates this with six practical cases from different chapters of fiqh, showing how the principle operates consistently across worship, financial obligations, and oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida
Extract the underlying principle: 'When in doubt about the obligation or its type, act on the greater as a precaution.' Note that this is a sughra (minor) maxim that complements the major maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt.'
The principle is derived from the cases, not stated explicitly in one sentence.
2
Understand the rationale
Recognize why akthar is chosen over aqall. The text explains that each unit (e.g., each fast) is an independent obligation; acting on the lesser leaves lingering worry. Caution removes that worry by ensuring all possible obligations are fulfilled.
This reasoning is crucial for the fatwa on qada fasts.
3
Apply to the first three furuat
Walk through the cases: missed prayer (pray a full day and night), zakat on mixed livestock (pay for all types), number of qada fasts (fast the larger number). Confirm that each follows the same logic of preferring the greater possible obligation.
These involve independent units (prayers, days, animal types).
4
Apply to the next two furuat (iddah and nadhr)
For iddah of unknown type (divorce vs. death), observe the longer period. For an unspecified vow (nadhr), if the type is unknown, render kaffarah yamin (expiation for an oath) because an unspecified vow is treated like an oath. This shows extension to non-worship contexts.
The iddah case involves a single continuous obligation, but caution still dictates the longer period.
5
Analyze the sixth furu' (oath) and the commentator's note
If one forgets whether an oath was by Allah, divorce, or manumission, the oath is invalid. Divorce/manumission cannot take effect with doubt; for an oath by Allah, the principle of original innocence (bara'at al-dhimmah) applies. The commentator flags that this case requires deeper reflection—it is an exception where caution points to invalidity rather than obligation.
This furu' shows that the qawida has limits; when doubt is about the very nature of the instrument, caution may void it.

Source Text

مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس پر اور روزے والے پر اکثر کولازم کیا جائے اور یہ فقہاء کے اس قول سے ماخوذ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کوئی ایک نماز چھوڑ دی اور اس میں شک ہے کہ وہ کون سی نماز ہے تو احتیاط پر عمل کرتے ہوئے اس پر ایک دن ایک رات کی نمازیں لازم ہوں گی ۔
تشریح کسی کے پاس مختلف اجناس کے سائمہ جانور ہیں اور اسے شک ہے کہ اس نے تمام کی زکاۃ نکالی
ہے یا بعض کی ؟ تو بقول مصنف اس کے لئے مناسب یہ ہے کہ تمام اجناس کے جانوروں کی زکاۃ نکالے۔ الثالث : کسی شخص کو قضا روزوں کی تعداد میں شک ہے کہ کتنے روزوں کی قضاء اس کے ذمہ ہے تو ایسے شخص کے لئے حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ متیقن روزوں کی قضاء کرے مثلاً پانچ یا سات میں شک ہے تو سات کی قضاء کرے۔ لیکن اس پر ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ اقل منیقین ہے تو اس پر عمل کرے یعنی پانچ پر جیسے نماز اس کی نظیر ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہر روز مستقل عبادت ہے اور مستقل فرض ہے اقل پر عمل کرنے میں قلب میں بقیہ کے بارے میں فکر رہے گی تو احتیاط کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ اکثر پر عمل کرے ۔
الرابع: عورت کو طلاق ووفاۃ میں سابق ومؤخر کا علم نہیں اور اس بات میں تردد ہے کہ آیا اس پر عدہ طلاق
واجب ہے یا عدۃ وفات تو اس کو چاہئے کہ آخرالا جلین زائد مدت جس میں درکار ہو وہ عدت گزارے۔ مذکورہ بالا صورتوں میں اسی طرح احتیاط پر عمل کیا گیا جیسے کسی کی ایک نماز چھوٹ گئی لیکن یہ معلوم نہیں کہ کون سی چھوٹی ہے؟ تو احتیاطاً ایک دن اور ایک رات کی نماز قضا کرے۔
الْخَامِسُ شَكٍّ فِي الْمَنْدُوْرِهَلْ هُوَ صَلوةٌ أَمْ صِيَامٌ أَوْ عِتْقُ أَوْ صَدَقَةً يَنْبَغِي أَنْ تَلْزَمَهُ كَفَّارَةُ يَمِيْنِ اعْذَا مِنْ قَوْلِهِمْ لَوْ قَالَ عَلَى نَدْرٌ فَعَلَيْهِ كَفَّارَةُ يَمِيْن لأنَّ الشَّك فى المنذور كَعَدَمِ تَسْمِيَّةِ السَّادِسُ شَكَ حَلَفَ بِاللهِ أَوْ بِالطَّلَاقِ أَوْ بِالْعِتَاقِ فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُوْنَ بَاطِلاً ثُمَّ رَأَيْتُ الْمَسْئِلَةَ فِي الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ فِي شَكٍّ الأَيْمَان حَلَفَ وَ نَسِيَ أَنَّهُ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ بِالطَّلَاقِ أَوْ بِالْعِناقِ فَحَلْقُهُ بَاطِل إنتهى.
:ترجمه: پانچواں جزئیہ جس چیز کی نذر مانی اس میں شک ہوا کہ وہ نماز ہے یار روز دیا غلام آزاد کر تایا صدقہ تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس پر کفارہ یمین لازم ہو اور یہ فقہاء کے اس قول سے ماخوذ ہے کہ اگر اس نے صرف یہ کہا علی نذر تو اس پر کفارہ یمین لازم ہے اس لئے کہ شئے منذور میں شک کا ہونا متعین نہ کرنے کے درجہ میں ہے۔ چھٹا جزئیہ شک ہوا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی قسم کھائی ہے یا طلاق کی یا عتاق کی؟ تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ وہ (حلف ) باطل ہو پھر میں نے بزازیہ میں ایمان میں شک کی بحث میں دیکھا کہ کسی نے قسم کھائی اور یہ بھول گیا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی قسم تھی یا طلاق کی یا عتاق کی تو اس کی قسم پائل ہے۔
تشریح کسی کو نذر ماننا تو یقین سے معلوم ہے البتہ منذور کے بارے میں شک ہے کہ وہ نماز ہے یا روزہ ؟ تو اسے چاہئے کہ کفارہ یمین ادا کرے اور مشکوک فیہ امور کا لعدم شمار ہوں گے کیونکہ مطلق نذر کی صورت میں کفارہ یمین لازم ہوتا ہے۔
شک هل حلف باللہ: ایک شخص کو اتنا یاد ہے کہ نے تم کھاتی ہے البت کس چیز کی تم کھائی طاق کی یا عتناق کی یا اللہ تعالیٰ کی یہ یاد نہیں ہے تو اس کی قسم لغو ہے یعنی اس پر کوئی کفارہ نہ آئے گا کیونکہ طلاق وعتاق شک کی حالت میں واقع نہیں ہوتے اور حلف باللہ کے بارے میں یہ بات ہے کہ اصل براۃ ذمہ ہے اس لئے کہ شک ہے اور شک کے ساتھ کفارہ لازم نہیں ہوتا شارح فرماتے ہیں کہ اس تفصیل میں غور کی ضرورت ہے۔
It is appropriate that the greater (akthar) be obligated upon him and upon the fasting person, and this is derived from the statement of the jurists that if someone missed one prayer and is uncertain which prayer it was, then acting with caution, a day and night's prayers are obligated upon him. Explanation: If someone has grazing animals of different types and is uncertain whether he paid zakat for all or some, according to the author it is appropriate that he pay zakat for all types. Third: If a person is uncertain about the number of qada fasts he owes, e.g., five or seven, he should fast the greater number (seven) because each day is an independent act of worship; acting on the lesser leaves worry in the heart. Fourth: If a woman does not know whether her iddah is due to divorce or death, she should observe the longer of the two periods. Fifth: If uncertain whether a vow is for prayer, fasting, freeing a slave, or charity, he should offer kaffarah yamin (expiation for an oath). Sixth: If uncertain whether he swore by Allah, divorce, or manumission, the oath is invalid; I saw in al-Bazzaziyyah that one who swore and forgot the type, his oath is null. The fifth case is derived from the scholars' statement that one who says 'upon me a vow' without specification owes kaffarah yamin. The sixth case: if uncertain, the oath is invalid. Commentary: For a vow, if the type is uncertain, one must offer kaffarah yamin because unspecified vows carry kaffarah. For an oath by Allah, doubt prevents obligation because of the principle of original innocence. The commentator says this detail needs reflection.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a collection of furuat (applications) derived from a general principle of caution in cases of doubt. The author begins by stating that when there is doubt about the exact obligation, one should act on the greater (akthar) to ensure fulfillment. He then provides six cases: (1) missed prayer of unknown identity – offer a full day and night of prayers; (2) zakat on multiple types of grazing animals – pay zakat for all types; (3) number of qada fasts – fast the larger number (seven if between five and seven); (4) type of iddah – observe the longer period; (5) nature of a vow (nadhr) – offer kaffarah yamin, as an unspecified vow is like an oath; (6) type of oath – if one forgets whether it was by Allah, divorce, or manumission, the oath is void, because divorce and manumission cannot take effect with doubt, and for an oath by Allah, the principle of original innocence (bara'at al-dhimmah) applies. The commentator adds that the sixth case requires further analysis, and notes the distinction between doubt in the oath itself and doubt in the object of the oath.

Key Terms
شک (shakk): Uncertainty between two possibilities, one of which is not more likely.
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Taking the more cautious course to ensure fulfillment of an obligation.
اقل (aqall): The smallest number or amount that is certain.
اکثر (akthar): The greater number or amount, which is more cautious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is uncertain whether he missed 5 or 7 qada fasts. According to the Hanafi principle of caution described in this passage, what should he do?
A) Pray istikhara and decide
B) Fast only 5, the certain number
C) Fast 7, the greater number
D) Fast 6 as a middle ground

Key Takeaway
When doubt arises about the type or quantity of an obligation, Hanafi caution requires acting on the greater possible obligation to ensure complete fulfillment, unless the doubt undermines the instrument itself.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
6 min
The Maxim 'Al-Asl al-'Adam' and Its Applications
Defines the maxim 'al-asl al-‘adam' and applies it to two marriage disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-asl al-‘adam' to identify whose statement is accepted in disputes about the occurrence of an event and state the exception for essential attributes.

Core Idea
The default is non-existence; the denier prevails without proof.

This lesson introduces one of the five major Hanafi maxims: 'al-asl al-‘adam' (the origin is non-existence). Understanding this maxim is crucial for resolving disputes in marriage and other contracts. The passage defines the maxim, clarifies its scope (applies to accidental attributes, not essential ones), and applies it to two specific cases from marriage law. You will learn to identify when this maxim governs and when it is overridden by the exception for essential attributes.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Memorize the Arabic phrase 'الأَصْلُ الْعَدَمُ' and understand that it applies to accidental attributes (ṣifāt ‘āriḍa), not essential attributes (ṣifāt aṣāliyya). For essential attributes, existence is the origin.
Essential attributes include life, knowledge, etc. The exception is grounded in the maxim 'al-yaqinu la yazulu bil-shakk'.
2
Identify claimant and defendant
In any dispute, the one who claims existence (contrary to the origin) is the claimant/mudda‘ī; the one who denies it is the defendant/mudda‘ā ‘alayh.
The defendant's statement with an oath is accepted; the claimant must bring proof.
3
Apply burden of proof
The claimant bears the burden of proof (bayyinah). The defendant's statement (with yamīn) is accepted because it aligns with the origin of non-existence.
4
Analyze the first application (impotence case)
If a husband claims intercourse and the wife denies, women examine her. If she is a virgin, the wife's denial aligns with the origin (no intercourse), so her statement is accepted and she has the option to separate. If she is a non-virgin, the husband's denial of impotence aligns with the origin (freedom from impotence), so his statement is accepted.
The wife is the defendant regarding intercourse; the husband is the defendant regarding his own impotence.
5
Analyze the second application (timing of separation)
After separation, if the wife says it occurred after consummation and the husband says before, the wife's statement is accepted because she denies the fall of half the mahr. The origin is that half the mahr is still due (non-existence of its drop).
The wife is the defendant regarding the dropping of mahr.

Source Text

خُيِّرَتْ وَإِنْ قُلْنَ ثَيِّبٌ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهُ لِكَوْنِهِ مُنْكِرًا إِسْتِحْقَاقَ الْفُرْقَةِ عَلَيْهِ وَ الأصْلُ السَّلَامَةُ مِنَ الْعَنَةِ وَ فِي الْقِنْيَةِ إفْتَرَقَا وَقَالَتْ إِفْتَرَقْنَا بَعْدَ الدُّخُولِ وَقَالَ الزَّوْجُ قَبْلَهُ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهَا لِأَنَّهَا تُنْكِرُ سُقُوْطَ نِصْفَ الْمَهْرِ إنْتَهى. ترجمه: قاعدہ اصل نہ ہونا ہے اور ذیل میں چند جزئیات ہیں ان میں سے یہ ہے کہ وطی کی نفی کرنے والوں کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ اصل عدم ہے لیکن عنین کے بارے میں فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر اس نے وطی کا دعویٰ کیا اور بیوی نے انکار کیا اور عورتوں نے بتایا کہ یہ باکرہ ہے تو اسے اختیار Maxim: The origin is non-existence. It has branches. Among them is that the statement of the one who denies intercourse is accepted because the origin is non-existence. But they said about the impotent man ('innin): If he claims intercourse and she denies, and women say she is a virgin, she has the option; and if they say she is a non-virgin, then his statement is accepted because he is denying that separation is due upon him, and the origin is freedom from impotence. And in al-Qunyah: They separated, and she said 'We separated after consummation,' and the husband said 'Before it,' then her statement is accepted because she denies the falling of half the dowry — end. Translation: The maxim is that the origin is non-existence, and below are some applications. Among them is that the word of the one who denies intercourse is accepted because the origin is non-existence. But regarding the impotent man, the jurists say: If he claims intercourse and she denies, and women report that she is a virgin, she is given the option; and if they say she is a non-virgin, then his statement is accepted because he denies that separation is due upon him, and the origin is that he is free from impotence. In al-Qunyah: The spouses separated; the wife said 'We separated after consummation,' and the husband said 'Before it,' then the wife's statement is accepted because she denies the fall of half the mahr. End. Explanation: The origin of a thing is non-existence. Only Allah's essence is real; all other things exist by His permission and creation. In everything besides Allah's essence, the origin is that it is temporal and non-existent, but this origin of non-existence is not absolute; it applies only to accidental attributes; in essential attributes, existence is the origin. As you learned, the origin is non-existence and existence is against the origin. Therefore, the one who claims against the origin must provide proof (bayyinah). And the one whose claim aligns with the origin is the defendant, and his statement with his oath is accepted. If the spouses dispute about whether intercourse occurred, the one who denies it has his statement accepted, with his oath, because the origin is non-existence of the thing, and the claimant of intercourse must provide proof. However, they said regarding the 'innin: If the husband says he performed intercourse and the wife denies, and women say she is a virgin, then the statement of the wife is accepted and she gets the option of separation; if they say she is a non-virgin, then the husband's statement is accepted, because the husband is denying that separation is due, and the origin is that he is free from impotence. In al-Qunyah: Separation occurred; the wife says 'We separated after consummation,' the husband says 'Before it,' then the wife's statement is accepted because she denies the fall of half the mahr.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage presents the major maxim 'Al-asl al-‘adam' (the origin is non-existence). It clarifies that in fiqh, the default state of affairs is that a thing does not exist, especially for accidental attributes. The one who claims existence (e.g., intercourse) must bring proof, while the one who denies it (thus aligning with the origin) has his statement accepted with an oath. The maxim then provides two applications (furu‘). First, in the case of an impotent man ('innin): if he claims intercourse and the wife denies, the physical examination by women determines whose statement prevails. If she is found to be a virgin, the wife's statement is accepted and she has the option to separate; if she is a non-virgin, the husband's statement is accepted (because the origin is that he is not impotent). Second, from al-Qunyah: after separation, if the spouses dispute whether the separation occurred before or after consummation, the wife's statement is accepted because she denies that half the mahr is dropped (since the origin is that half the mahr is still due).

Key Terms
اصل العدم (asl al-‘adam): The legal principle that the default state of affairs is non-existence for accidental matters.
عنین ('innin): A man who is impotent and cannot perform intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute about whether intercourse occurred, whose statement is accepted according to the maxim 'al-asl al-‘adam'?
A) The husband who claims it occurred.
B) The wife who denies it occurred.
C) Both statements are equal.
D) It requires witness testimony.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'al-asl al-‘adam' places the burden of proof on the one claiming existence; the denier's statement is accepted with an oath.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

The Maxim al-Asl al-‘Adam and Its Application in Property Disputes
Enumerating applications of the maxim al-Asl al-‘Adam in disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maxim al-asl al-‘adam and apply it to resolve disputes regarding whether a transfer was a loan, trust, gift, or usurpation.

Core Idea
When in doubt, the default is non-existence; the one claiming an exception must prove it.

This lesson introduces the fundamental Hanafi legal maxim 'al-asl al-‘adam' (the original state is non-existence). We will see how this maxim resolves common disputes in property transactions: whether a transfer was a loan, trust, gift, or usurpation. The maxim places the burden of proof on the one who asserts a deviation from the default.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the maxim
The maxim al-asl al-‘adam means that in any dispute, the default position is that the claimed event or condition did not occur. The party affirming its existence bears the burden of proof.
2
Examine the loan vs mudaraba dispute
After the property is destroyed, if the owner says it was a loan and the taker says mudaraba, the owner's statement is relied upon because the original is non-loan (i.e., the default is that the transfer was not a loan unless proven otherwise).
3
Examine trust vs usurpation dispute
If the taker says it was a trust and the owner says usurpation, the taker is liable because the original is non-trust (so the taker must prove trust). But if the taker says it was given as trust and the owner says usurpation, the taker is not liable because the original is non-usurpation.
4
Examine gift vs loan dispute
The giver says it was a loan, the taker says a gift. The giver's statement is relied upon because the original is non-gift (i.e., the default is that the transfer was not a gift).
5
Synthesize the pattern
In all these disputes, the maxim al-asl al-‘adam determines whose statement is reliable: the one who asserts the absence of the claimed transfer (loan, trust, gift) or the presence of a harmful transfer (usurpation) is believed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: اور یہی حکم اس کے ہلاک ہو جانے کے بعد ہے اس لئے کہ مالک کا یہ قول معتبر ہے کہ وہ مال بطور قرض ہے عنایہ وغیرہ میں ایساہی ہے اور اسی وجہ سے کنز میں ہے اگر کسی نے کہا کہ میں نے تجھ سے ایک ہزار ودیعت کے طور پر لئے اور وہ ہلاک ہو گئے اور مالک نے کہا کہ تو نے بطور غصب لئے تھے تو وہ ضامن ہوگا اور اگر اس نے کہا کہ تو نے مجھے وہ بطور ودیعت دیئے تھے اور مالک نے کہا کہ وہ تو نے غصب کئے تھے تو وہ ضامن نہیں ہوگا کنز کا کلام پورا ہوا۔ اور بزاز یہ میں ہے کسی نے دوسرے کو کچھ سامان دیا پھر دونوں میں اختلاف ہوا اور دینے والے نے کہا کہ وہ قرض ہے اور دوسرے نے کہا کہ ہدیہ ہے تو دینے والے کا قول معتبر ہوگا بزاز یہ کا کلام پورا ہوا اس لئے کہ دعوی کرنے والا قیمت سے بری کئے جانے کا دعوی کر رہا ہے حالانکہ وہ سامان فی نفقہ مال متقوم ہے۔ تشریح اگر مال کے ہلاک ہونے کے بعد اختلاف ہوا رب المال کہتا ہے کہ میں نے بطور قرض دیا تھا اور لائن کہتا ہے کہ بطور مضاربت دیا تھا تو ایسی صورت میں رب المال کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ آخذ نے کہا میں نے تجھ سے ایک ہزار روپے بطور امانت لئے تھے وہ ہلاک ہو گئے اور رب الممال کہہ رہا ہے تو نے غصب کر کے رکھ لئے تھے تو انیسی صورت میں آخذ ضامن ہوگا۔ و في البزازية دفع لاخر : ایک شخص نے دوسرے کو کوئی سامان دیا اور دونوں میں اختلاف ہو گیا دینے والا کہتا ہے کہ یہ قرض ہے اور لینے والا کہتا ہے یہ ہدیہ ہے تو دینے والے کی بات معتبر ہوگی کیونکہ جبہ کا دعویٰ کرنے والا قیمت سے بری ہونے کا دعویٰ کر رہا ہے حالانکہ وہ سامان بذات خود متقوم ہے۔ وَمِنْهَا لَوْ أَدْخَلَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ حِلْمَةَ تَدْيِهَا فِي فَمِ الرَّضِيْعَ وَلَا يَدْرِى أَدْخَلَ اللَّيْنِ فِي خَلْقِهِ أمْ لَا لَا يَحْرُمُ النِّكَاحُ لأنَّ فِي الْمَائِعِ شَكَّا كَذَا فِي الْوَلْوَالِحِيَّةِ وَ سَيَانِي تَمَامُهُ فِي قَاعِدَةِ أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ فِي الْأَبْضَاعِ الْحُرْمَةُ ترجمه : اور الاصل العدم کی جزئیات میں ہی سے ہے اگر عورت نے اپنی پستان کی گھنڈی دودھ پیتے بچہ کے منھ میں ڈالی اور اسے یہ معلوم نہیں کہ دودھ اس کے حلق میں گیا ہے یا نہیں تو نکاح حرام نہیں ہوگا اس لئے کہ مائع میں شک ہے والوالجہ میں ایساہی ہے اور اس کی پوری تفصیل عنقریب قاعدہ الاصل فی الا بضاع الحرمۃ کے ذیل میں آئے گی۔ تشریح کسی عورت نے اپنی پستان کی گھنڈی بچہ کے منھ میں ڈالدی لیکن دودھ اتر نا معلوم نہیں تو محض بچہ کے منھ میں پستان کی گھنڈی ڈالنے سے اور دودھ کے شک سے حرمت رضاعت ثابت نہ ہوگی لہذاوہ بچہ حرام نہیں ہوگا۔ وَمِنْهَا لَوْ اخْتَلَفَا فِي قَبْضِ الْمَبِيْعِ أَوِ الْعَيْنِ الْمُوْجَرَةِ فَالْقَوْلُ لِمُنْكِرِهِ كَمَا فِي إِجَارَةِ الْهَدَيْبِ وَ مِنْهَا لَوْ ثَبَتَ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنَ بِاقْرَارِ أَوْ بَيْنَةٍ فَادَّعى الأَدَاءَ أَوِ الإِبْرَاءَ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلدَّائِمِ لأَنَّ الأَصْلَ الْعَدَمُ وَمِنْهَا لَوْ إِخْتَلَفَا فِي قِدَمِ الْعَيْب فَأَنْكَرَهُ الْبَائِعُ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهُ وَاخْتَلَفَ فِي تَعْلِيْلِهِ فَقِيْلَ لأنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُه وَ قِيْلَ لأنَّ الأصْلَ لُزُوْمُ الْعَقْدِ. ترجمہ: اور ان یعنی الاصل العدم کی جزئیات میں ہی سے ہے اگر دو آدمیوں میں مبیع کرائے پر دیئے گئے کسی مین پر قبضہ کرنے میں اختلاف ہوا تو اس کے منکر کا قول معتبر ہو گا التہذیب کے باب الاجارہ میں ایسا ہی ہے ۔ اور اسی کی جزئیات میں سے ہے اگر کسی پر اقرار یا بینہ کے ذریعہ قرض ثابت ہو گیا پھر اس نے ادا کر دینے یا بری کئے جانے کا ھوٹی کیا تو قرض دہندہ کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس لئے کہ اصل ادا یا بری نہ کیا جاتا ہے اور اسی کا جزئیہ ہے اگر عیب کے قدیم ہونے میں اختلاف ہوا اور بائع نے اس کا انکار کیا تو اسی کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اس کی علت میں اختلاف ہے کہا گیا کہ اصل اس (عیب) کا نہ ہونا ہے اور ایک قول یہ ہے کہ اصل عقد کا لازم نہ ہونا ہے۔ تشریح : بائع اور مشتری کے مابین اختلاف ہوا کہ قبضہ ہوا ہے یا نہیں تو ایسی صورت میں جو قبضہ کے ہونے کا منکر ہے اس کی بات معتبر ہے۔ ومنها ما لو ثبت دین باقرار : ایک شخص کے ذمہ دین ثابت ہو گیا پھر اس نے دعوی کیا کہ وہ ادا کر چکا ہے اور دائن کہتا ہے کہ نہیں کیا تو دائن کی بات معتبر ہو گی کیونکہ اصل عدم ادا اور عدم ابراء ہے۔ لو اختلـفـا في قديم العیب : بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان عیب کے متعلق اختلاف ہوا بائع کہتا ہے کہ عیب پہلے نہیں تھا مشتری کہتا ہے کہ عیب پہلے سے تھا تو اب بائع کی بات معتبر ہوگی کیونکہ اصل عیب کا نہ ہونا ہے۔ وَمِنْهَا لَوْ اخْتَلَفَا فِي اشْتِرَاطِ الْخِيَارِ فَقِيْلَ الْقَوْلُ لِمَنْ نَفَاهُ عَمَلًا بِأَنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُهُ وَ قِيْلَ لِمَنِ ادَّعَاهُ لأَنَّهُ يُنْكِرُ لُزُوْمَ الْعَقْدِ وَ قَدْ حَكَيْنَا الْقَوْلَيْنِ فِي الشَّرْحِ وَالْمُعْتَمَدُ الأَوَّلُ وَمِنْهَا لَوْ قَالَ غَصَبْتُ مِنْكَ أَلْفًا وَ رَبَحْتُ فِيْهَا عَشَرَةَ اللَافٍ فَقَالَ الْمَغْصُوبُ مِنْهُ بَلْ كُنْتُ أَمَرْتُكَ بِالتِّجَارَةِ بِهَا فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْمَالِكِ كَمَا فِي إِقْرَارِ الْبَرَّازِيَّةِ يَعْنِي لِتَمَسُّكِهِ بِالْأَصْلِ وَهُوَ عَدَمُ الْعَصْبِ وَ مِنْهَا لَوِ اخْتَلَفَا فِي رُؤْيَةِ الْمَسْعِ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْمُشْتَرِي لأَنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُهَا وَلَوِ اخْتَلَفَا فِي تَغَيرِ الْمَبِيْعِ بَعْدَ رُؤْيَتِهِ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْبَائِعِ لأنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُ التغير.
Translation: And the same ruling applies after its destruction, because the owner's statement is reliable that the property was a loan. It is similar in Inayah etc. And for this reason in Kanz: if someone said 'I took one thousand from you as a trust and they were destroyed' and the owner said 'you took them as usurpation', then he is liable; and if he said 'you gave them to me as a trust' and the owner said 'you usurped them', then he is not liable. The speech of Kanz is complete. And in Bazzaziyyah: someone gave something to another, then they disputed; the giver said it was a loan, the other said a gift; then the giver's statement is reliable. The speech of Bazzaziyyah is complete because the claimant is claiming to be free from value, while the property is valuable in itself. Explanation: If after destruction they disputed, the owner says 'I gave as a loan' and the taker says 'as mudaraba', then the owner's statement is reliable. The taker said 'I took one thousand rupees from you as a trust and they were destroyed' and the owner says 'you usurped them', then in this case the taker is liable. And in Bazzaziyyah: one person gave something to another and they disputed; the giver says it is a loan, the taker says it is a gift; then the giver's statement is reliable because the claimant is claiming to be free from value, while the property is valuable in itself. And among them: if a woman put her nipple into the mouth of an infant and it is not known whether milk entered his stomach or not, marriage is not prohibited because there is doubt about the liquid. So in Walwaljiyyah. And its complete discussion will come under the principle 'The original in private parts is prohibition'. Explanation: A woman put her nipple into the mouth of a child but it is not known whether milk descended, then merely putting the nipple in the mouth and doubt about milk do not prove foster relationship prohibition, so the child is not prohibited. And among them: if they dispute about delivery of the sold item or the rented item, then the statement of the denier is reliable, as in Ijarah of al-Hadayb. And among them: if a debt is proven against someone by confession or evidence, then he claims payment or discharge, then the statement of the creditor is reliable because the original is non-existence. And among them: if they dispute about the pre-existence of a defect and the seller denies it, then his statement is reliable; and there is difference in its rationale: it is said because the original is its non-existence, and it is said because the original is the binding nature of the contract. Translation: And among these (sub-cases of 'the original is non-existence') is: if two people dispute about delivery of a sold item or a rented item, then the statement of the denier is reliable, as in al-Tahdhib, chapter of Ijarah. And among its sub-cases: if a debt is proven against someone by confession or evidence, then he claims payment or discharge, then the statement of the creditor is reliable because the original is non-payment and non-discharge. And among its sub-cases: if they dispute about the pre-existence of a defect and the seller denies it, then his statement is reliable; and there is difference in its rationale: it is said because the original is its non-existence, and it is said because the original is the binding nature of the contract. Explanation: seller and buyer dispute whether delivery occurred; then the one who denies delivery, his statement is reliable. Among them: if a debt is proven against someone by confession or evidence, then he claims he has paid and the creditor says no, then the creditor's statement is reliable because the original is non-payment and non-discharge. They dispute about pre-existence of defect: seller says defect was not there before, buyer says it was there before; then the seller's statement is reliable because the original is non-existence of defect. And among them: if they dispute about stipulation of option, then it is said the statement of the one who denies it is reliable, acting on the principle that the original is its non-existence; and it is said the statement of the one who claims it is reliable because he denies the binding nature of the contract, and we have mentioned both opinions in the commentary, and the relied-upon is the first. And among them: if someone said 'I usurped one thousand from you and profited ten thousand in it' and the usurpee said 'but I had ordered you to trade with it', then the statement of the owner is reliable as in Iqrar of Bazzaziyyah, meaning because he holds to the original, which is the absence of permission. And among them: if they dispute about sight of the purchased item, then the statement of the buyer is reliable because the original is its absence. And if they dispute about change of the purchased item after sight, then the statement of the seller is reliable because the original is no change.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a collection of furuat (applications) of the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-asl al-‘adam' (the original state is non-existence). The author presents these as sub-cases from the chapter on qawaid. The maxim means that in any dispute, the default is that the claimed event or condition did not occur, and the burden of proof lies on the one asserting its existence. The examples cover various fiqh chapters:

Key Terms
الأصل العدم (al-asl al-‘adam): A legal maxim meaning that the default presumption in any matter is non-existence; the burden of proof lies on the one claiming existence.
فروع (furua): Sub-cases or applications of a legal principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute where the owner claims a transfer was a loan and the taker claims it was mudaraba, after the property is destroyed, whose statement is reliable according to al-asl al-‘adam?
A) The taker's, because he has possession
B) The owner's, because the original is non-loan
C) The taker's, because mudaraba is valid
D) The owner's, because he is the owner

Key Takeaway
The maxim al-asl al-‘adam places the burden of proof on the party asserting the existence of a fact, making it a critical tool for resolving disputes in property transactions.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
12 min
Applications of al-Asl al-‘Adam in Contracts and Family Law
Enumerating applications of the maxim al-Asl al-‘Adam in disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim al-asl al-‘adam to resolve disputes in sales, ijarah, debt payment, defect, option, sight, and foster nursing.

Core Idea
The maxim al-‘adam resolves contract and family disputes by presuming non-existence of the claimed event.

This lesson continues the furuat of al-asl al-‘adam, covering applications in sales contracts (delivery, defect, option, sight) and a family law case regarding foster nursing. In each, the maxim dictates whose statement is reliable, ensuring consistency in legal presumptions.

Guided Path
1
Examine dispute over delivery (qabd)
If buyer and seller dispute whether the sold item was delivered, the one denying delivery is believed because the original is non-delivery.
2
Examine dispute over debt payment
If a creditor and debtor dispute whether the debt was paid or discharged, the creditor's statement is relied upon because the original is non-payment.
3
Examine dispute over pre-existing defect
If seller and buyer dispute whether a defect was present before sale, the seller's denial is believed because the original is no defect.
There is a secondary rationalization: the original is the binding nature of the contract.
4
Examine dispute over option (khiyar)
If parties dispute whether a stipulation of option was made, the one denying it is believed, acting on the maxim. An alternative opinion exists but the relied-upon view is the first.
5
Examine foster nursing case
If a woman puts her nipple in an infant's mouth but it is unknown if milk entered, marriage is not prohibited because the original is non-ingestion of milk.
This is a different context but still applies the same maxim.
6
Examine other disputes: sight, change, usurpation with permission
In disputes about sight of the purchased item, the buyer's claim of non-sight is believed. In disputes about change after sight, the seller's claim of no change is believed. In a usurpation case where the taker claims permission, the owner's denial of permission is believed.

کہتا ہے یہ ہدیہ ہے تو دینے والے کی بات معتبر ہوگی کیونکہ جبہ کا دعویٰ کرنے والا قیمت سے بری ہونے کا دعویٰ کر رہا ہے حالانکہ وہ سامان بذات خود متقوم ہے۔ وَمِنْهَا لَوْ أَدْخَلَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ حِلْمَةَ تَدْيِهَا فِي فَمِ الرَّضِيْعَ وَلَا يَدْرِى أَدْخَلَ اللَّيْنِ فِي خَلْقِهِ أمْ لَا لَا يَحْرُمُ النِّكَاحُ لأنَّ فِي الْمَائِعِ شَكَّا كَذَا فِي الْوَلْوَالِحِيَّةِ وَ سَيَانِي تَمَامُهُ فِي قَاعِدَةِ أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ فِي الْأَبْضَاعِ الْحُرْمَةُ ترجمه : اور الاصل العدم کی جزئیات میں ہی سے ہے اگر عورت نے اپنی پستان کی گھنڈی دودھ پیتے بچہ کے منھ میں ڈالی اور اسے یہ معلوم نہیں کہ دودھ اس کے حلق میں گیا ہے یا نہیں تو نکاح حرام نہیں ہوگا اس لئے کہ مائع میں شک ہے والوالجہ میں ایساہی ہے اور اس کی پوری تفصیل عنقریب قاعدہ الاصل فی الا بضاع الحرمۃ کے ذیل میں آئے گی۔ تشریح کسی عورت نے اپنی پستان کی گھنڈی بچہ کے منھ میں ڈالدی لیکن دودھ اتر نا معلوم نہیں تو محض بچہ کے منھ میں پستان کی گھنڈی ڈالنے سے اور دودھ کے شک سے حرمت رضاعت ثابت نہ ہوگی لہذاوہ بچہ حرام نہیں ہوگا۔ وَمِنْهَا لَوْ اخْتَلَفَا فِي قَبْضِ الْمَبِيْعِ أَوِ الْعَيْنِ الْمُوْجَرَةِ فَالْقَوْلُ لِمُنْكِرِهِ كَمَا فِي إِجَارَةِ الْهَدَيْبِ وَ مِنْهَا لَوْ ثَبَتَ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنَ بِاقْرَارِ أَوْ بَيْنَةٍ فَادَّعى الأَدَاءَ أَوِ الإِبْرَاءَ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلدَّائِمِ لأَنَّ الأَصْلَ الْعَدَمُ وَمِنْهَا لَوْ إِخْتَلَفَا فِي قِدَمِ الْعَيْب فَأَنْكَرَهُ الْبَائِعُ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهُ وَاخْتَلَفَ فِي تَعْلِيْلِهِ فَقِيْلَ لأنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُه وَ قِيْلَ لأنَّ الأصْلَ لُزُوْمُ الْعَقْدِ. ترجمہ: اور ان یعنی الاصل العدم کی جزئیات میں ہی سے ہے اگر دو آدمیوں میں مبیع کرائے پر دیئے گئے کسی مین پر قبضہ کرنے میں اختلاف ہوا تو اس کے منکر کا قول معتبر ہو گا التہذیب کے باب الاجارہ میں ایسا ہی ہے ۔ اور اسی کی جزئیات میں سے ہے اگر کسی پر اقرار یا بینہ کے ذریعہ قرض ثابت ہو گیا پھر اس نے ادا کر دینے یا بری کئے جانے کا ھوٹی کیا تو قرض دہندہ کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس لئے کہ اصل ادا یا بری نہ کیا جاتا ہے اور اسی کا جزئیہ ہے اگر عیب کے قدیم ہونے میں اختلاف ہوا اور بائع نے اس کا انکار کیا تو اسی کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اس کی علت میں اختلاف ہے کہا گیا کہ اصل اس (عیب) کا نہ ہونا ہے اور ایک قول یہ ہے کہ اصل عقد کا لازم نہ ہونا ہے۔ تشریح : بائع اور مشتری کے مابین اختلاف ہوا کہ قبضہ ہوا ہے یا نہیں تو ایسی صورت میں جو قبضہ کے ہونے کا منکر ہے اس کی بات معتبر ہے۔ ومنها ما لو ثبت دین باقرار : ایک شخص کے ذمہ دین ثابت ہو گیا پھر اس نے دعوی کیا کہ وہ ادا کر چکا ہے اور دائن کہتا ہے کہ نہیں کیا تو دائن کی بات معتبر ہو گی کیونکہ اصل عدم ادا اور عدم ابراء ہے۔ لو اختلـفـا في قديم العیب : بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان عیب کے متعلق اختلاف ہوا بائع کہتا ہے کہ عیب پہلے نہیں تھا مشتری کہتا ہے کہ عیب پہلے سے تھا تو اب بائع کی بات معتبر ہوگی کیونکہ اصل عیب کا نہ ہونا ہے۔ وَمِنْهَا لَوْ اخْتَلَفَا فِي اشْتِرَاطِ الْخِيَارِ فَقِيْلَ الْقَوْلُ لِمَنْ نَفَاهُ عَمَلًا بِأَنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُهُ وَ قِيْلَ لِمَنِ ادَّعَاهُ لأَنَّهُ يُنْكِرُ لُزُوْمَ الْعَقْدِ وَ قَدْ حَكَيْنَا الْقَوْلَيْنِ فِي الشَّرْحِ وَالْمُعْتَمَدُ الأَوَّلُ وَمِنْهَا لَوْ قَالَ غَصَبْتُ مِنْكَ أَلْفًا وَ رَبَحْتُ فِيْهَا عَشَرَةَ اللَافٍ فَقَالَ الْمَغْصُوبُ مِنْهُ بَلْ كُنْتُ أَمَرْتُكَ بِالتِّجَارَةِ بِهَا فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْمَالِكِ كَمَا فِي إِقْرَارِ الْبَرَّازِيَّةِ يَعْنِي لِتَمَسُّكِهِ بِالْأَصْلِ وَهُوَ عَدَمُ الْعَصْبِ وَ مِنْهَا لَوِ اخْتَلَفَا فِي رُؤْيَةِ الْمَسْعِ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْمُشْتَرِي لأَنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُهَا وَلَوِ اخْتَلَفَا فِي تَغَيرِ الْمَبِيْعِ بَعْدَ رُؤْيَتِهِ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْبَائِعِ لأنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُ التغير.
Translation: And the same ruling applies after its destruction, because the owner's statement is reliable that the property was a loan. It is similar in Inayah etc. And for this reason in Kanz: if someone said 'I took one thousand from you as a trust and they were destroyed' and the owner said 'you took them as usurpation', then he is liable; and if he said 'you gave them to me as a trust' and the owner said 'you usurped them', then he is not liable. The speech of Kanz is complete. And in Bazzaziyyah: someone gave something to another, then they disputed; the giver said it was a loan, the other said a gift; then the giver's statement is reliable. The speech of Bazzaziyyah is complete because the claimant is claiming to be free from value, while the property is valuable in itself. Explanation: If after destruction they disputed, the owner says 'I gave as a loan' and the taker says 'as mudaraba', then the owner's statement is reliable. The taker said 'I took one thousand rupees from you as a trust and they were destroyed' and the owner says 'you usurped them', then in this case the taker is liable. And in Bazzaziyyah: one person gave something to another and they disputed; the giver says it is a loan, the taker says it is a gift; then the giver's statement is reliable because the claimant is claiming to be free from value, while the property is valuable in itself. And among them: if a woman put her nipple into the mouth of an infant and it is not known whether milk entered his stomach or not, marriage is not prohibited because there is doubt about the liquid. So in Walwaljiyyah. And its complete discussion will come under the principle 'The original in private parts is prohibition'. Explanation: A woman put her nipple into the mouth of a child but it is not known whether milk descended, then merely putting the nipple in the mouth and doubt about milk do not prove foster relationship prohibition, so the child is not prohibited. And among them: if they dispute about delivery of the sold item or the rented item, then the statement of the denier is reliable, as in Ijarah of al-Hadayb. And among them: if a debt is proven against someone by confession or evidence, then he claims payment or discharge, then the statement of the creditor is reliable because the original is non-existence. And among them: if they dispute about the pre-existence of a defect and the seller denies it, then his statement is reliable; and there is difference in its rationale: it is said because the original is its non-existence, and it is said because the original is the binding nature of the contract. Translation: And among these (sub-cases of 'the original is non-existence') is: if two people dispute about delivery of a sold item or a rented item, then the statement of the denier is reliable, as in al-Tahdhib, chapter of Ijarah. And among its sub-cases: if a debt is proven against someone by confession or evidence, then he claims payment or discharge, then the statement of the creditor is reliable because the original is non-payment and non-discharge. And among its sub-cases: if they dispute about the pre-existence of a defect and the seller denies it, then his statement is reliable; and there is difference in its rationale: it is said because the original is its non-existence, and it is said because the original is the binding nature of the contract. Explanation: seller and buyer dispute whether delivery occurred; then the one who denies delivery, his statement is reliable. Among them: if a debt is proven against someone by confession or evidence, then he claims he has paid and the creditor says no, then the creditor's statement is reliable because the original is non-payment and non-discharge. They dispute about pre-existence of defect: seller says defect was not there before, buyer says it was there before; then the seller's statement is reliable because the original is non-existence of defect. And among them: if they dispute about stipulation of option, then it is said the statement of the one who denies it is reliable, acting on the principle that the original is its non-existence; and it is said the statement of the one who claims it is reliable because he denies the binding nature of the contract, and we have mentioned both opinions in the commentary, and the relied-upon is the first. And among them: if someone said 'I usurped one thousand from you and profited ten thousand in it' and the usurpee said 'but I had ordered you to trade with it', then the statement of the owner is reliable as in Iqrar of Bazzaziyyah, meaning because he holds to the original, which is the absence of permission. And among them: if they dispute about sight of the purchased item, then the statement of the buyer is reliable because the original is its absence. And if they dispute about change of the purchased item after sight, then the statement of the seller is reliable because the original is no change.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a collection of furuat (applications) of the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-asl al-‘adam' (the original state is non-existence). The author presents these as sub-cases from the chapter on qawaid. The maxim means that in any dispute, the default is that the claimed event or condition did not occur, and the burden of proof lies on the one asserting its existence. The examples cover various fiqh chapters:

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Delivery; taking possession of a sold item.
خيار (khiyar): Option; right to rescind a contract.
رضاع (rada'): Foster nursing; milk relationship causing marriage prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over whether a sold item was sighted before purchase, who is believed according to al-asl al-‘adam?
A) The seller, because he knows the item
B) The buyer, because the original is non-sight
C) Both, the contract is void
D) The one who has witnesses

Key Takeaway
The maxim al-‘adam provides a consistent default for resolving diverse disputes across contracts and family law by presuming non-existence of the claimed event.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
10 min
The Default is Non-Existence: Distinguishing Accidental from Original Attributes
Explaining the qawida with its nuance and applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'al-asl al-adam' with its distinction between original and accidental attributes to determine whose statement is accepted in a dispute, using the furuat provided.

Core Idea
The default is non-existence only for accidental attributes; for original attributes, the default is existence.

This lesson refines a common legal maxim. At first glance, 'the default is non-existence' seems universal, but Hanafi jurists limit it to attributes that can be acquired or lost. Attributes inherent in creation are presumed to exist. Understanding this distinction is crucial for resolving disputes in sales, options, and emancipation.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida and its qualification
Learn the Arabic text of the maxim and its limiting dabt (sub-maxim). Recognise that the maxim is not absolute.
The dabt is: الأصل العدم مطلقا إنما هو في الصفات العارضة، وأما في الصفات الأصلية فالوجود.
2
Distinguish accidental from original attributes
Identify the criteria: accidental attributes (e.g., baking, writing, seeing) can be acquired or lost and are not part of the thing's creation. Original attributes (e.g., virginity, limbs, innate qualities) are inherent.
Use the legal_definition_dissector for 'الصفات العارضة' to understand the components.
3
Apply to sales disputes (khiyar and condition)
Work through the examples: khiyar al-shart (denier believed), khiyar al-ru'yah (buyer believed on not seeing, seller believed on change), condition of baker/writer (buyer believed), condition of virginity (seller believed).
Each case maps to either accidental (default non-existence) or original (default existence).
4
Apply to emancipation by condition
Cases: master says 'Every baker slave is free' – slave claims baker, master denies; master says 'Every virgin slave-girl is free' – slave-girl claims virgin, master denies. The outcome depends on the attribute type.
Baker = accidental, virgin = original.
5
Identify the underlying rationale (talil)
Understand why the rule exists: certainty (originals are certain at creation) vs. uncertainty (accidentals are changeable). This connects to the related qawida 'al-yaqin la yazul bi al-shakk'.
This strengthens the application in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کئے اور ان میں دس ہزار روپے کا نفع ہوا ہے اس پر جس کا مال غصب کیا گیا اس نے کہا بلکہ میں نے تجھے ان سے تجارت کا حکم دیا تھا تو مالک کا قول معتبر ہوگا بزاز یہ کے کتاب الاقرار میں ایسا ہی ہے یعنی اس کے اصل کو اختیار کرنے کی وجہ سے اور وہ (اصل) غصب کا نہ ہوتا ہے اور ایک جزئیہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مبیع کی رؤیت میں اختلاف ہوا تو مشتری کا قول معتبر گا اس لئے کہ اصل اس ( رؤیت) کا نہ ہوتا ہے اور اگر میچ کو دیکھ لینے کے بعد اس میں تبدیلی ہو جانے کے سلسلہ میں اختلاف ہوا تو بائع کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس لئے کہ اصل متغیر نہ ہونا ہے۔
تشریح خیار شرط عقد میں لگایا تھا یا نہیں اس سلسلہ میں اختلاف ہوا تو ایسی صورت میں جو خیار شرط کا منکر
ہے اس کی بات معتبر ہوگی کیونکہ اصل خیار شرط کا نہ ہونا ہے۔ لو قال غصبت منک الفا: ایک شخص نے کہا کہ میں نے تیرے ایک ہزار روپے غصب کئے تھے اس میں نفع ہوا ہے دس ہزار روپے کا اور مالک کہتا ہے کہ میں نے تجھے روپے تجارت کے لئے دیئے تھے تو مالک کی بات مانی جائے گی کیونکہ وہ اصل عدم غصب کا مدعی ہے۔
لو إختلفا في رؤية المبيع: عقد میں خیار رویت ثابت ہونے کے بعد رؤیت ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں اختلاف ہوا مشتری کہتا ہے کہ میں نے مبیع نہیں دیکھی تو مشتری کی بات قبول کی جائے گی۔ ولو إختلفا في تغير المبيع: خیار رویت کی صورت میں مشتری نے مبیع کو دیکھنے کے بعد دعویٰ کیا کہ مبیع بدل چکی ہے بائع انکار کر رہا ہے تو بائع کی بات معتبر ہوگی کیونکہ اصل عدم تغیر ہے۔
لَيْسَ الأَصْلُ الْعَدَمُ مُطْلَقاً وإِنَّمَا هُوَ فِى الصِّفَاتِ الْعَارِضَةِ وَ أَمَّا فِي الصِّفَاتِ الأَصْلِيَةِ
فَالأَصْلُ الْوُجُودُ. ترجمه: تنبيه قاعدة الاصل العدم مطلقا نہیں ہے یہ صرف صفات عارضہ میں ہے صفات اصلیہ میں اصل وجود ہے۔ تشریح: اشیاء کا معدوم ہونا اصل جو بتایا گیا ہے یہ صفات عارضہ کے بارے میں ہے رہی بات صفات اصلیہ کی جو خلقہ شئی میں موجود ہو تو ان میں اصل چیز یہ ہے کہ وہ چیز موجود ہے۔
وَتَفَرَّعَ عَلَيْ ذَلِكَ أَنَّهُ لَوِ اشْتَرَاهُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَّارٌ أَوْ كَاتِبٌ وَ انْكَرَ وَجُوْدَ ذَلِكَ الْوَصْفِ به فَالْقَوْلُ لَهُ لأنَّ الأَصْلَ عَدَمُهَا لِكَوْنِهِمَا مِنَ الصَّفَاتِ الْعَارِضَةِ وَ لَوِاشْتَرَاهَا عَلَىٰ أَنَّهَا بِكُرُ وَ انْكَرَ قِيَامَ الْبَكَارَةِ وَ ادَّعَاهُ الْبَائِعُ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْبَائِعِ لَأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ وَجُودُهَا لِكَوْنِهَا صِفَةً أَصْلِيَّةٌ كَذَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيْرِ مِنْ خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ وَ عَلَى هَذَا تَفَرَّعَ لَوْ قَالَ كُلُّ مَمْلُوْفٍ لِي خَبَّارٌ فَهُوَ حُرِّ فَادَّعَاهُ عَبْدٌ وَ انْكَرَ الْمَوْلَى فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْمَوْلَى ترجمہ: اور اس پر متفرع ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اسے یعنی غلام کو اس طرح پر خریدا کہ وہ روٹی پکانا جانتا ہے یا کا تب ہے اور مشترکی نے اس میں ان اوصاف کا انکار کیا تو اس (مشتری) کا قول معتبر ہوگا اس لئے کہ اصل ان دونوں کا نہ ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ دونوں صفاتِ عارضہ میں سے ہیں اور اگر کسی نے اس شرط پر باندی خریدی کہ وہ یا کرو ہے اور مشتری نے بکارت کے باقی رہنے سے انکار کیا اور بائع نے اس (قیام بکارت ) کا دعویٰ کیا تو بائع کا قول معتبر ہے اس لئے کہ اصل اس کا ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ صفت اصلیہ ہے۔ فتح القدیر کی خیار شرط کی بحث میں ایسا ہی ہے اور اس پر متفرع ہے اگر مولی نے کہا کہ میرا ہر وہ غلام جو روٹی بنانا جانتا ہو آزاد ہے کسی غلام نے اس کا نان بائی ہونے ) کی دعوی کیا اور آقا ء نے انکار کیا تو آقا ء کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
تشریح : اصل عدم ہے اس پر تفریح بیان کی جارہی ہے کہ ایک شخص نے غلام خریدا اس شرط پر کہ وہ نان بائی ہے یا کا تب ہے لہندا بائع کہتا ہے کہ وہ خباز ہے یا کا تب ہے اور مشتری اس کا انکار کرتا ہے تو مشتری کا قول معتبر ہوگا اس لئے کہ نان بائی ہونایا کا تب ہو نا صفات عارضہ میں سے ہے جو کہ اصل نہ ہونا ہے۔ ولو اشتراها على انها بکر : ایک شخص نے باندی با کرہ ہونے کی شرط پر خریدی پھر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ یہ با کرو نہیں ہے اور بائع کہتا ہے کہ یہ باکرہ ہے تو بائع کی بات معتبر ہوگی نہ کہ مشتری کی کیونکہ بکارت صفات اصلیہ میں سے ہے کذافی فتح القدير و على هذا تفرع لو قال کل مملوک لی : آقا ء نے کہا کہ میرا ہر نان بائی غلام آزاد ہے پھر ایک غلام نے نان بائی ہونے کا دعویٰ کیا اور آقا اس کا منکر ہے تو آقا ء کی بات معتبر ہوگی کیونکہ اصل صفات عارضہ کا نہ ہوتا ہے۔ وَلَوْ قَالَ كُلُّ جَارِيَةٍ بِكُر لى فَهِيَ حُرَّةً فَادَّعَتْ جَارِيَةٌ أَنَّهَا بِكُرٌ وَ انْكَرَ الْمَوْلَىٰ فَالْقَوْلُ لَهَا وَ تَمَامُ تَفْرِيعِهِ فِي شَرْجِنَا عَلَى الكنز فِي تَعْلِيقِ الطَّلَاقِ عِنْدَ شَرْح قَوْلِهِ وَ إِنْ اخْتَلَفَا في وجود الشرط.
ترجمہ: اور اگر کہا میری ہر کنواری باندی آزاد ہے ایک باندی نے دعوی کیا کہ وہ کنواری ہے اور مولی منکر ہے تو باندی کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اس کی پوری تفریحات کنز پر ہماری شرح کی تعلیق طلاق کے باب میں اس قول کی شرح کے موقع پرو إن اختلفا في وجود الشرط کے مقام پر بیان کی گئی ہے۔ تشریح مولیٰ نے اپنی باندیوں کو مخاطب کر کے کہا کہ باکرہ باندی آزاد ہے تو ایک باندی نے اپنے باکرہ ہونے کا دعوی کیا تو یہاں پر باندی کی بات ہی معتبر ہوگی نہ کہ موٹی کی کیونکہ یہ صفات اصلیہ میں سے ہے جس میں اصل وجود ہے۔
قَاعِدَةُ : الأَصْلُ إضَافَةُ الْحَادِثِ إِلَى اقْرَبِ أَوْقَاتِه مِنْهَا مَا قَدَّمْنَاهُ فِيْمَا لَوْ رَاع فِي تَوْبِهِ نِجَاسَةٌ وَ قَدْ صَلَى فِيْهِ وَلَا يَدْرِكْ مَتى أَصَابَتْهُ يُعِيدُهَا مِنْ أخِرِ حَدَثٍ أَحْدَثَهُ وَ الْمَنِي مِنْ
[Continuation from previous page] ... he made and there was a profit of ten thousand rupees, the person whose property was usurped said: 'Rather, I had ordered you to trade with them.' So the owner's statement will be accepted. Al-Bazzaziyyah in Kitab al-Iqrar says similarly: because he chooses the default (al-asl), and that default is non-usurpation. Another example: if there is a dispute regarding seeing the merchandise, the buyer's statement will be accepted because the default is non-seeing. And if after seeing the merchandise there is a dispute about a change, the seller's statement will be accepted because the default is no change. Explanation: If there is a dispute about whether an option of condition was stipulated in the contract, the one who denies the option of condition's statement will be accepted because the default is no option of condition. If someone says: 'I usurped one thousand dirhams from you, and there was a profit of ten thousand dirhams,' and the owner says: 'I gave you the money for trade,' then the owner's statement will be accepted because he claims the default of non-usurpation. If they dispute about seeing the merchandise: after the option of sight is established, if they dispute whether the merchandise was seen or not, the buyer says he did not see it, so the buyer's statement will be accepted. And if they dispute about a change in the merchandise: in the case of option of sight, the buyer claims that the merchandise has changed, the seller denies, so the seller's statement will be accepted because the default is no change. 'The default is not absolutely non-existence; rather it is regarding accidental attributes. As for original attributes, the default is existence.' Translation: A note: The rule 'al-asl al-adam' is not absolute; it is only in accidental attributes; in original attributes, the default is existence. Explanation: What was stated that the default of things is non-existence, this is regarding accidental attributes. As for original attributes that are inherent in the creation of a thing, the default is that the thing is present. And derived from this: if one buys a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a writer, and the buyer denies the existence of that attribute, then the statement is his (the buyer's) because the default is their non-existence, as they are from accidental attributes. And if one buys a slave-girl on the condition that she is a virgin, and the buyer denies the existence of virginity, and the seller claims it, then the statement is the seller's because the default is its existence, as it is an original attribute. Similarly in Fath al-Qadir from the chapter of option of condition. And on this is derived: if someone says, 'Every slave of mine who is a baker is free,' and a slave claims that he is a baker and the master denies, then the statement is the master's. Translation: And derived from this: if someone bought him—meaning a slave—on the condition that he knows how to bake bread or is a writer, and the buyer denies these attributes, then his (the buyer's) statement will be accepted because the default of both is non-existence, as both are from accidental attributes. And if someone bought a slave-girl on the condition that she is a virgin, and the buyer denies the existence of virginity, and the seller claims it, then the seller's statement is accepted because the default is its existence, as it is an original attribute. Similarly in Fath al-Qadir in the discussion of option of condition. And on this is derived: if the master said, 'Every slave of mine who knows how to bake bread is free,' and a slave claims that he is a baker and the master denies, then the master's statement will be accepted. Explanation: The default is non-existence. Applications are being discussed: A person bought a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a writer. So the seller says he is a baker or writer, and the buyer denies. Then the buyer's statement is accepted because being a baker or writer is among accidental attributes, whose default is non-existence. And if he bought her on condition that she is a virgin: A person bought a slave-girl on the condition of virginity, then later found that she is not a virgin, and the seller says she is a virgin, then the seller's statement is accepted, not the buyer's, because virginity is among original attributes. Similarly in Fath al-Qadir. And on this is derived: if the master said, 'Every baker slave of mine is free,' then a slave claims he is a baker and the master denies, then the master's statement is accepted because the default of accidental attributes is non-existence. And if he said, 'Every virgin slave-girl of mine is free,' and a slave-girl claims that she is a virgin and the master denies, then the statement is hers. And the complete derivation of this is in our commentary on al-Kanz in the chapter of ta'liq al-talaq at the explanation of his statement: 'And if they dispute about the existence of the condition.' Translation: And if he said, 'Every virgin slave-girl of mine is free,' and a slave-girl claims that she is a virgin and the master denies, then the slave-girl's statement is accepted, and its full derivations are explained in our commentary on al-Kanz in the chapter of ta'liq al-talaq at the explanation of the statement 'and if they dispute about the existence of the condition.' Explanation: The master addressed his slave-girls saying that a virgin slave-girl is free. So a slave-girl claimed her virginity. Here the slave-girl's statement is accepted, not the master's, because this is from original attributes, in which the default is existence. Rule: The default is to attribute an event to its nearest time. Among its examples is what we presented earlier regarding if someone finds najasah on his garment and he prayed in it and does not know when it struck him, he repeats from the last defilement he had.
